# Thylacine OS — Technical Reference

This document is the **as-built** reference for Thylacine OS. It describes what exists in the tree today, where the relevant code lives, which formal specs pin which invariants, and how the subsystems compose. It is NOT a roadmap and NOT a design document — see `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` for design intent and `docs/ROADMAP.md` for phased scope.

---

## How to read this

The reference is split by subsystem, one file per layer of the stack. Each file follows the same template:

- **Purpose** — one paragraph on what the layer does and where it sits in the stack.
- **Public API** — every exported function with its contract.
- **Implementation** — structure + invariants + known caveats.
- **Spec cross-reference** — formal modules that pin invariants for this layer.
- **Tests** — which suites exercise the layer and what they cover.
- **Status** — what's implemented today vs. what's stubbed or deferred. Commit hashes cite the landing points.

When a section describes a detail enforced by a spec, the spec's action / invariant name is in `backticks`. When a section cites a file, the form is `path/to/file.c:line` so editors can jump there.

---

## Snapshot

- **Tip**: **P5-stratumd-stub-bringup audit close landed (substantive `bcd6fea` / hash fixup `1ae21e5`) — focused opus-prosecutor round across the e1 + e2 syscall + territory surfaces; 1 P0 / 1 P1 / 2 P2 / 3 P3 closed; **535/535 PASS × default + UBSan** (533 → 535).** **F1 [P0] kernel-stack info leak in SYS_WALK_OPEN**: pre-fix `char name_scratch[SYS_WALK_OPEN_NAME_MAX]` (64 B) + conditional NUL write (`if (name_len_raw < SYS_WALK_OPEN_NAME_MAX) name_scratch[name_len_raw] = '\0';`) — at `name_len_raw == 64` the NUL was never written; `dev9p_walk`'s strlen scan (`while (s[l] != '\0') l++;`) walked past the scratch into adjacent kernel stack until a 0 byte appeared. The discovered length packed into the Twalk wname[0] over the user-controlled transport, leaking saved registers / return addresses / KASLR slide. **Fixed by**: widening scratch to `SYS_WALK_OPEN_NAME_MAX + 1` bytes + unconditional NUL terminator. The Dev `walk` vtable has no length array — NUL is REQUIRED, not "defense-in-depth" (the misleading comment that allowed the bug is rewritten under F6). Regression test `sys_walk_open.max_length_name_nul_terminated`: a 64-byte name + custom loopback responder that asserts the wire `Twalk`'s wname[0]_len is EXACTLY 64; a regressed handler producing non-NUL-terminated scratch would over-scan and ship a larger length. **F2 [P1] closes R15 F236 (was deferred to "the SYS_WALK chunk")**: walked-Spoor UAF on Proc exit via handle-table ascending-index iteration. SYS_ATTACH_9P → SYS_CHROOT → SYS_WALK_OPEN(FROM_ROOT) → `t_exits` → `proc_free`'s `territory_unref` then `handle_table_free` ascending → `attach_fd` closes first → `dev9p_close(root)` → `p9_attached_destroy` → `kfree(client)` → walked_fd's subsequent close → `p9_client_clunk(stale_client, fid)` → UAF on `c->magic` at best, on `c->lock / c->session / c->transport` on SLUB slot recycling (worst case cross-session confusion). **Fixed by**: refcounting `p9_attached`. New API `p9_attached_ref / unref / install_transport`; legacy `p9_attached_destroy` retained as unref alias. `struct p9_attached` gains `ref` + `adapter` + `transport_tx` + `transport_rx`; ownership of adapter + transport Spoor refs transfers into the attached via `p9_attached_install_transport` (called by `sys_attach_9p_handler` after `p9_attached_create` succeeds). `dev9p_priv` loses `adapter_to_free` (now lives in attached); `attached_owner` semantics extended — EVERY priv (root + every walked) holds one ref. `priv_alloc` takes an `attached_owner` parameter and bumps on alloc; `dev9p_walk` propagates `src_priv->attached_owner` so walks inherit. `dev9p_close` is uniformized: clunk fid (fid_owned branch) THEN unref attached. The last unref runs the full teardown (clunk root_fid + p9_client_close + p9_client_destroy + free buffers + spoor_clunk tx/rx + kfree adapter + kfree a). The destroy-ordering invariant holds: `p9_client_close` calls `ops.close(adapter_ctx)` BEFORE the adapter is `kfree`'d. Regression test `p9_attached.walked_outlives_root_no_uaf`: simulates the syscall-path attached_owner stamp + walks via `dev9p.walk` + closes root BEFORE walked; pre-fix would UAF on `p9_client_clunk`. **F3 [P2] dev9p_walk allocation order**: pre-fix `p9_client_alloc_fid` ran before `walkqid_alloc` — a SLUB OOM on the latter consumed a fid from the monotonic counter without release. Reordered: walkqid first; fid-alloc failure now does `walkqid_free(w)`. **F4 [P2] `devramfs_walk` Dev-vtable contract violation**: latent — devramfs_walk discards the caller-supplied `nc` and sets `wq->spoor = cur` (own clone), but `sys_walk_open_handler` builds the whole walk around `nc` and assumes the reuse-nc shape. Defense at the call site: `if (w->spoor != nc) { walkqid_free(w); nc->aux = NULL; spoor_unref(nc); return -1; }`. Handler comment now documents the dev9p contract assumption + the future-Dev requirement. **F5 [P3] missing offset asserts on `Territory.root_spoor` / `binds` / `mounts`**: pre-fix only `sizeof(struct Territory)` was asserted; a future field reorder could shift offsets without changing total size. Added three `_Static_assert(__builtin_offsetof(...))` pins. **F6 [P3] misleading NUL-terminator comment**: rewrote — explicitly documents that NUL termination is REQUIRED for dev9p_walk's strlen scan, not "defense-in-depth". **F7 [P3] undocumented Dev-policy assumption in rights stamp**: extended comment to document the dev9p delegation + the future-Dev contract (returned rights MUST derive from source slot if the Dev's policy uses kernel rights for enforcement). **Captured-finding (e1 failure-path aux discipline) verified still in force**: walk-failure path (`nc->aux = NULL; spoor_unref(nc);`), open-failure path (`spoor_clunk(nc);`), handle_alloc-failure path (`spoor_clunk(nc);`) — 0 deviations. **Posture**: 535/535 PASS × default + UBSan (533 → 535; +2 regression tests for F1 + F2), 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Scripture**: this Snapshot entry; closed-list `memory/audit_p5_stratumd_stub_e1_e2_closed_list.md`; `audit_r15_closed_list.md` updated to record F236 closed. **Next**: sub-chunk f (real stratumd swap-in after Phase 6 musl sysroot). v1.x deferred: `pivot_root` / `SYS_UNCHROOT` so a long-running Proc can release a chroot mid-life. Predecessor: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-e2 (`d1e012c` / `470f32e`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-e2 landed (substantive `d1e012c` / hash fixup `470f32e`) — `SYS_CHROOT` syscall (= 35) + `Territory.root_spoor` field + `SYS_WALK_OPEN_FROM_ROOT == (u64)-1` sentinel land the v1.0 chroot mechanism per `CORVUS-DESIGN.md §10.1` (`"pivot_root (or chroot at v1.0; full pivot at v1.x)"`).** Sixth sub-chunk of the P5-stratumd-stub-bringup arc (a `479d997` userspace responder + 2-Proc kernel demo; b `73784b4` `SYS_SPAWN_WITH_FDS` + `/stub-driver`; c `6c1c816` joey-inline orchestration; d `cde54e8` stub serves synthetic FS; e1 `f37748b` `SYS_WALK_OPEN`; e2 THIS). The pickup doc's 3-option speculation (chroot vs bind-replace-root vs spawn-with-root) was redundant — CORVUS-DESIGN.md `§10.1 Q2` had already locked the v1.0 choice as chroot. **Kernel mechanism** (`kernel/territory.c::territory_chroot`, ~30 LOC): `(territory, source) → 0/-1`. Validates source non-NULL → idempotent same-pointer short-circuit (returns 0, no ref bump) → `spoor_ref(source)` BEFORE swap (so a corrupted source extincts cleanly, leaving root_spoor unchanged) → assign `territory->root_spoor = source` → if prior root existed, `spoor_clunk(old)` (NOT `spoor_unref` — MREPL-style displacement runs the Dev's close hook if this was the last holder). **`struct Territory` field**: new `struct Spoor *root_spoor` at offset 24 (between `_pad` and `binds[]`); `_Static_assert(sizeof(struct Territory) == 32 + 8*PGRP_MAX_BINDS + 16*PGRP_MAX_MOUNTS)` bumped from 24 to 32 header bytes. `territory_init_fields` sets NULL; `territory_clone` deep-copies + `spoor_ref` (each clone is its own holder); `territory_unref` final-release `spoor_clunk`s the root_spoor BEFORE `kmem_cache_free`. **New syscall `SYS_CHROOT = 35`** (`kernel/syscall.c::sys_chroot_handler`, ~25 LOC): thin SVC wrapper — `current_thread + current_proc + territory` non-NULL checks → `sys_lookup_spoor(p, fd, RIGHT_READ)` (same gate as `SYS_MOUNT`) → `territory_chroot(p->territory, source)`. **`SYS_WALK_OPEN` extension**: when `spoor_fd_raw == SYS_WALK_OPEN_FROM_ROOT == (u64)-1`, the handler resolves the source from `p->territory->root_spoor` instead of a handle (no `spoor_ref` — the Territory's existing reference keeps it alive across the syscall); if `root_spoor == NULL`, returns -1. **libt** (`usr/lib/libt/include/thyla/syscall.h`): `T_SYS_CHROOT = 35` + `t_chroot(spoor_fd) → 0/-1` inline wrapper + `T_WALK_OPEN_FROM_ROOT == (long)-1` constant. **`/stub-walk-probe` extension** (`usr/stub-walk-probe/stub-walk-probe.c`, +~60 LOC): after the existing e1 sequence (attach + walk_open(attach_fd) + read + EOF + close), appends the e2 sequence — `t_chroot(attach_fd) → 0` + `t_walk_open(T_WALK_OPEN_FROM_ROOT, "hello", 5, T_OREAD) → root_hello_fd` + `t_read` content-check + `t_read` EOF + `t_close`. Probe is a short-lived child Proc; its `t_exits(0)` releases the chroot via `territory_unref → spoor_clunk(root_spoor)` → adapter teardown → stub sees EOF → exits cleanly. **Joey-side**: explicit NOTE comment in `do_stratumd_stub_bringup` documenting why joey does NOT chroot — joey is the long-running init Proc; a chroot would hold the attach Spoor alive past `t_close(attach_fd)`, deadlocking `t_wait_pid` on a never-EOF'd stub (empirically confirmed during impl: the boot hung past 60s). v1.x adds `pivot_root` / `SYS_UNCHROOT` so a long-running Proc can release a chroot mid-life; until then chroot is one-way at v1.0. Joey blob cap raised 65 KiB → 128 KiB to accommodate the explanatory comment + future orchestration growth. **6 new kernel tests** in `kernel/test/test_territory_chroot.c`: `territory.chroot_smoke` / `_idempotent_same_spoor` / `_replace_clunks_old` / `_clone_bumps_ref` / `_destroy_drops_ref` / `_null_returns_error` — cover the full territory_chroot lifecycle in isolation (smoke + idempotent + MREPL-style replace + clone-propagation + final-release drop + NULL-source error). **Spec extension** (`specs/territory.tla`): new state variable `root_spoor : [Procs -> Spoors ∪ {NONE}]` (NONE = string sentinel, distinct from symbolic model values); new actions `Chroot(p, s)` (two-key EXCEPT updates refcount on both new + old, conditional on old being NONE) + `BuggyChrootNoRefbump(p, s)` (stamps root_spoor without bumping refcount); `ForkClone` extended to copy parent's root_spoor + bump refcount per-clone; `BuggyDestroyLeak` extended to also clear root_spoor; `MountRefcountConsistency` formula extended to `|MountEntriesForSpoor(s)| + |{p : root_spoor[p] = s}|`. New cfg `territory_buggy_chroot_no_refbump.cfg` produces the expected counterexample at depth 2 / 205 states. All 4 existing buggy cfgs still violate as expected — no regression. Per project-wide spec-to-code suspension (`141f9dd`), no clean-cfg TLC re-verification; buggy cfgs are the practical gate. **Audit-bearing** per CLAUDE.md §25.4 — touches `kernel/syscall.c` (new syscall entry point), `kernel/territory.c` (Territory: cycle-freedom, isolation, mount-refcount consistency), handle table (`sys_lookup_spoor`). VMO + scheduler + poll + notes + KASLR + ELF + mprotect + boot NOT touched. Self-audit clean — bump-before-swap discipline (corrupted source extincts before pointer change); idempotent same-source returns 0; MREPL-style spoor_clunk on displaced root; sentinel `(u64)-1` is unambiguous (hidx_t handles are non-negative); FROM_ROOT path does NOT spoor_ref the source (Territory's existing reference keeps it alive). A focused audit round bundling SYS_WALK_OPEN (e1 deferred) + SYS_CHROOT + the failure-path aux discipline is appropriate as the next deliverable. **Posture**: **533/533 PASS × default + UBSan** (527 → 533; +6 `territory.chroot_*` cases), 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Scripture**: `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md §11.2` row for `chroot(spoor_fd) → 0`; new `docs/reference/77-sys-chroot.md` deep-dive; `docs/reference/18-territory.md` extended (root_spoor field + territory_chroot API + extended MountRefcountConsistency + chroot tests + the one-way-at-v1.0 caveat); `docs/reference/61-stratumd-stub.md` extended with full e2 section + arc table updated. **Next**: focused audit round bundling SYS_WALK_OPEN (e1) + SYS_CHROOT + failure-path aux discipline (e1 trap captured in memory). Then sub-chunk f (real stratumd swap-in after Phase 6 musl sysroot). Predecessor: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-e1 (`f37748b` / `de8b389`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-e1 landed (substantive `f37748b` / hash fixup `de8b389`) — `SYS_WALK_OPEN` syscall + `t_walk_open` libt wrapper land the v1.0 minimum walk-through-mount primitive; new `/stub-walk-probe` validates the kernel 9P client + dev9p Dev vtable path end-to-end and joey reads `/hello` through the mount on every boot.** Fifth sub-chunk of the P5-stratumd-stub-bringup arc (a `479d997` userspace responder + 2-Proc kernel demo; b `73784b4` `SYS_SPAWN_WITH_FDS` + `/stub-driver`; c `6c1c816` joey-inline orchestration; d `cde54e8` stub serves synthetic FS; e1 THIS). **New syscall `SYS_WALK_OPEN = 34`** (`kernel/syscall.c::sys_walk_open_handler`, ~125 LOC): `(spoor_fd, name_va, name_len, omode) → opened_fd / -1`. Single-component walk: validates `name_len ∈ (0, SYS_WALK_OPEN_NAME_MAX=64]`, user-VA range, `omode` against `SYS_WALK_OPEN_OMODE_VALID=0x13` (low 2 bits + `OTRUNC`); looks up source Spoor with `RIGHT_READ`; rejects components containing `/`, `\0`, equal `.`, equal `..`; `spoor_clone(src)` → `nc`; `src->dev->walk(src, nc, [name], 1)` (on failure: detach `nc->aux` to skip the shared-aux UAF risk before `spoor_unref(nc)` — `dev9p_walk` only replaces aux on success); `walkqid_free` the carrier; `nc->dev->open(nc, omode)` (on failure: `spoor_clunk(nc)` runs the proper `dev9p_close` teardown that clunks the walk-allocated fid); `handle_alloc(p, KOBJ_SPOOR, R|W|TRANSFER, nc) → fd`. Rights envelope matches `SYS_ATTACH_9P`; the server enforces the actual omode at IO time. Dev-agnostic — dispatches through `dev->walk` + `dev->open`. **libt** (`usr/lib/libt/include/thyla/syscall.h`): `T_SYS_WALK_OPEN=34` + `t_walk_open(spoor_fd, name, name_len, omode) → fd` inline + omode constants (`T_OREAD=0`, `T_OWRITE=1`, `T_ORDWR=2`, `T_OEXEC=3`, `T_OTRUNC=0x10`) + `T_WALK_OPEN_NAME_MAX=64`. **NEW `usr/stub-walk-probe/stub-walk-probe.c`** (~85 LOC): `t_attach_9p(0, 1, "/", 1, 0) → attach_fd` → `t_walk_open(attach_fd, "hello", 5, T_OREAD) → hello_fd` → `t_read(hello_fd, buf, 64)` must return 25 + content bytewise-equal `"hello from stratumd-stub\n"` → second `t_read` at offset 25 must return 0 (EOF) → close both → `t_exits(0)`. **New kernel test** `userspace.stratumd_stub_walk_round_trip` (`kernel/test/test_stratumd_stub.c`): mirror of `fs_round_trip` but client is `/stub-walk-probe`; tests coexist (raw-9P wire vs kernel-client+Dev-vtable+new-syscall). **`usr/joey/joey.c::do_stratumd_stub_bringup`**: inserts `t_walk_open + t_read + content-check + t_close(hello_fd)` between the existing `t_unmount(99)` and `t_close(attach_fd)` calls. Success diagnostic now `joey: stub-bringup ok (pipe + spawn + attach + mount + unmount + walk_open + read)`. Every boot exercises `SYS_WALK_OPEN` end-to-end. **Scripture**: `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md §11.2` gains a row for `walk_open(spoor_fd, name, omode) → opened_fd`; `docs/reference/61-stratumd-stub.md` gains the full e1 sub-chunk section (Scope, Kernel surface, libt surface, Probe, Joey-inline, Kernel test wiring, Test count, Audit-trigger surfaces touched); Status table + Known caveats updated; sub-chunk arc table at the top now shows e1 LANDED + e2 (territory-root pivot) DEFERRED. **No spec change** — `SYS_WALK_OPEN` is composition over the already-spec'd 9P client + handle + Spoor layers (`9p_client.tla` already pins fid lifecycle + tag uniqueness; `handles.tla` already pins KOBJ_SPOOR rights). **Audit-bearing** per CLAUDE.md §25.4 — touches kernel/syscall.c (every syscall entry point is in the trigger list), handle table (`handle_alloc`), 9P client (transitively via `dev->walk` + `dev->open`). Territory + VMO + scheduler + poll + notes + KASLR + ELF + mprotect are NOT touched. Self-audit clean — strict component-shape validation (`/`, `\0`, `.`, `..` rejected); right-required gate on source fd; vtable-presence check; the failure-path detach-aux-then-unref discipline that avoids the shared-aux UAF (dev9p_close on a Spoor with src's aux would clunk src's fid); spoor_clunk on the post-walk pre-open and post-open paths runs the proper teardown for either state. A focused audit round on the syscall + the joey-inline + the probe is appropriate before promoting to non-stub callers. **Posture**: **527/527 PASS × default + UBSan** (526 → 527; +1 `userspace.stratumd_stub_walk_round_trip`), 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Reference**: `docs/reference/61-stratumd-stub.md` extended with full e1 section; `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md §11.2` row added. **Next**: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-e2 — territory-root pivot (kernel mechanism so the mounted Spoor becomes the joey territory's root). Three design options on the table (chroot-shape; bind-replace-root; spawn-with-root). All three cross `territory.c` (audit-trigger), so e2 lands as its own sub-chunk with a focused audit. Then f (real stratumd swap-in after Phase 6 musl sysroot). Predecessor: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-d (`cde54e8` / `016e20d`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-d landed (substantive `cde54e8` / hash fixup `016e20d`) — stratumd-stub serves a synthetic FS (Twalk + Tlopen + Tread over `/hello`); new `/stub-fs-probe` raw-9P client validates walk + open + read end-to-end.** Fourth sub-chunk of the P5-stratumd-stub-bringup arc (a `479d997` userspace responder + 2-Proc kernel demo; b `73784b4` `SYS_SPAWN_WITH_FDS` + `/stub-driver`; c `6c1c816` joey-inline orchestration; d THIS). **Stub extension** (`usr/stratumd-stub/stratumd-stub.c`): tiny 16-slot per-session fid table (`fid_id`, `path`, `opened` per entry) + new wire handlers. Synthetic FS = root (qid path=1, QTDIR) + one file `/hello` (qid path=2, QTFILE, content `"hello from stratumd-stub\n"` 25 bytes). Tattach now parses `fid` + allocates a root-bound slot (was: ignored). Twalk supports `nwname=0` (clone) + `nwname=1, name="hello"` from root; same-fid walks replace in place per 9P semantics; anything else → Rlerror ENOENT. Tlopen marks the fid open (flags ignored at v1.0; read-only). Tread on `/hello` returns the requested slice (count-clamped to remaining); EOF returns `count=0` (NOT an error); reading the directory → Rlerror EISDIR. Tclunk frees the slot (idempotent). **New companion binary** (`usr/stub-fs-probe/stub-fs-probe.c`, ~280 LOC): mirror-image userspace 9P CLIENT driving Tversion + Tattach + Twalk("hello") + Tlopen + Tread + Tread@EOF + Tclunk×2 over raw pipes (the kernel test pre-installs `c2s_wr` at fd 0, `s2c_rd` at fd 1). Probe asserts: Rwalk's qid type == QTFILE; Rread first call returns 25 bytes byte-for-byte == HELLO_CONTENT; Rread second call (offset=25) returns count=0. **New kernel test** (`kernel/test/test_stratumd_stub.c::test_stratumd_stub_fs_round_trip`): structurally identical to the existing `stratumd_stub_round_trip` test but client is `/stub-fs-probe`. Both tests coexist (handshake-only vs walk-open-read coverage of the same stub). **Why raw-9P probe (not t_attach_9p + walk-through-mount)**: at v1.0 Thylacine has no userspace walk/open syscall that reaches into a dev9p-backed Spoor's underlying 9P fid table (only `t_srv_connect` does walk-and-open, and that's /srv-specific). Raw bytes through pipes is the minimum-scope path to exercise the new wire handlers without inventing a new syscall; sub-chunk e (territory-root pivot + walk primitive) is the natural place for joey-side walk-through-mount semantics. No spec change — composition over the already-spec'd 9P client + pipe + handle layers. No new audit-trigger surface — the stub + probe are userspace test fixtures; the kernel-side wire codec was audited at the P5-wire / -session chunks. Self-audit clean — fid-table table-full + duplicate-bind guards; EBADF on unbound fids; opened-bit check on Tread; bounded BUF_MAX=512 with response-cap checks before every put_u32; Rlerror builder shared so every error path symmetrically renders the correct envelope. **Posture**: **526/526 PASS × default + UBSan** (525 → 526; +1 `userspace.stratumd_stub_fs_round_trip`), 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Reference**: `docs/reference/61-stratumd-stub.md` updated with sub-chunk d's full design + status + caveats. **Next**: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-e — territory-root pivot (kernel mechanism to substitute a mounted Spoor as joey's `/`) + a userspace walk-through-mount primitive so joey reads `/sysroot/hello` directly without raw 9P encoding. Then f (real stratumd swap-in after Phase 6 musl sysroot). Predecessor: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-c (`6c1c816` / `712308d`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-c landed (substantive `6c1c816` / hash fixup `712308d`) — joey runs the `/stub-driver` orchestration inline on the production boot path.** Third sub-chunk of the P5-stratumd-stub-bringup arc (a `479d997` userspace responder + 2-Proc kernel demo; b `73784b4` `SYS_SPAWN_WITH_FDS` + `/stub-driver` standalone orchestrator binary; c THIS). The same joey-shape sequence — `t_pipe ×2 → t_spawn_with_fds → t_close ×2 → t_attach_9p → t_mount → t_unmount → t_close ×3 → t_wait_pid` — moves from the standalone `/stub-driver` test binary into a new `do_stratumd_stub_bringup()` static in `usr/joey/joey.c`, called after the corvus-d hybrid-PKE arc finishes. `target_path_id = 99` matches `/stub-driver`'s convention to keep the kernel-test and boot-path mount-table identifiers aligned. **Value-add over (b)**: production-shape evidence on the actual boot log (not a separate test binary); every boot now exercises `SYS_ATTACH_9P` + `SYS_MOUNT` end-to-end, so regressions in those surfaces become boot-time signals; the line that says "boot pivot is possible" moves from a self-contained kernel-test artifact onto the same boot path that runs corvus. **What it does not yet do**: reads through the mount (the stub returns Rlerror on Twalk, so `dev_walk` into the mount fails — that's sub-chunk d, which adds Twalk + Tlopen + Tread to a small synthetic FS); doesn't make `/sysroot` joey's namespace root (sub-chunk e: territory-root pivot); doesn't use real stratumd (sub-chunk f: swap-in after Phase 6's musl sysroot lands). **No spec change** — pure composition over the already-spec'd 9P client + pipe + handle + mount layers. **No audit-trigger surface** — joey is a userspace orchestrator; the cap / uaccess / mount paths it touches are already audited. Self-audit clean — failure semantics return -1 with a `joey: stub-bringup ... FAILED` diagnostic, treated as a boot regression; refcount discipline mirrors `/stub-driver` exactly (joey drops c2s_rd + s2c_wr immediately after `t_spawn_with_fds` so the stub sees EOF when joey closes its tx). **Posture**: 525/525 PASS × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors (no kernel-test count change — the integration validation runs as part of the existing boot test). **Reference**: `docs/reference/61-stratumd-stub.md` updated with the c sub-chunk + revised arc / status / caveats sections. **Next**: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup-d — extend the stub to serve Twalk + Tlopen + Tread over a tiny synthetic FS (e.g., one file `/hello` returning a fixed string) so joey can read content through the mount end-to-end. Then e (territory-root pivot), then f (real stratumd). Predecessor: P5-hostowner-b-b (`ef14dbc` / `a3f4e1b`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-hostowner-b-b landed (substantive `ef14dbc` / hash fixup `a3f4e1b`) — corvus `ADMIN_ELEVATE` + joey redemption + `USER_CREATE` admin gate.** Second + final sub-chunk of P5-hostowner-b. The userspace consumer of the `cap` device from b-a. **`ADMIN_ELEVATE` verb (verb_id=7)** in `usr/corvus/src/main.rs::handle_admin_elevate`: verifies session-token validity → console-attached peer (via cached `conn.peer.console`; immutable, kernel-stamped, never rfork-propagated) → system passphrase EQUALS `SYSTEM_PASSPHRASE` (v1.0 PLACEHOLDER: hardcoded `"thylacine"` byte-compare; real Argon2id+AEAD-wrap mechanism per CORVUS-DESIGN.md §5.5 lands when CRVS persistence does) → registers a pending grant for `conn.peer.stripes` via the new `SYS_CAP_GRANT` syscall. **`joey`** then calls **`t_cap_use(T_CAP_HOSTOWNER)`** (new `SYS_CAP_USE` syscall) — joey's Proc gains `CAP_HOSTOWNER` on success. **Admin-verb gating** (the C-22 pattern): new `peer_live_caps(handle)` helper issues a fresh `t_srv_peer` per call (never caches caps on per-conn state); `handle_user_create` now requires `peer_live_caps(handle) & CAP_HOSTOWNER != 0`. **Bootstrap exception**: the first `USER_CREATE` while the user table is empty is allowed without the cap — closes the chicken-and-egg (ADMIN_ELEVATE needs an authenticated session, which needs a user, which needs USER_CREATE, which needs CAP_HOSTOWNER, which needs ADMIN_ELEVATE). Single-threaded corvus → no TOCTOU on the `user_states_count() > 0` check. **joey** confers `T_CAP_GRANT_HOSTOWNER` on corvus in the spawn mask (alongside `T_CAP_LOCK_PAGES` + `T_CAP_CSPRNG_READ`); the kernel's `cap_register_grant_for_writer` gate-checks this fork-grantable cap. **joey's revised boot sequence**: USER_CREATE michael (bootstrap) → AUTH wrong → AUTH ok → ADMIN_ELEVATE → t_cap_use → USER_CREATE susan (gated, passes) → WRAP / UNWRAP × 5 / SESSION_CLOSE / Q11 reconnect (unchanged). **Two new syscalls** (`SYS_CAP_GRANT=32` + `SYS_CAP_USE=33`): direct userspace bridges to `cap_register_grant_for_writer` / `cap_redeem_grant_for_writer` — the eventual production path is the Dev write op on `/cap/grant` / `/cap/use` through a future namespace-aware `t_open`; these syscalls are the v1.0 alternative front-end and converge on the same kernel cores (identical gate semantics). **libt** + **libthyla-rs** get `T_CAP_HOSTOWNER` (1 << 3) + `T_CAP_GRANT_HOSTOWNER` (1 << 4) constants + `t_cap_grant` / `t_cap_use` wrappers. **The corvus-d audit's deferred F2-gate-half** (USER_CREATE not CapHostowner-gated; the gate "lands with ADMIN_ELEVATE / P5-hostowner-b" was its closing condition) is now **CLOSED**. **No spec change** — `specs/corvus.tla::AdminElevate` + `AdminRequiresProcCap` + `HostownerRequiresConsole` already model the mechanism. Per the project-wide spec-to-code suspension (`141f9dd`), no clean-cfg TLC re-verification; buggy cfgs remain GREEN. **Audit-bearing** per CLAUDE.md §25.4 (kernel syscall.c additions + capability mutation in cap_redeem_grant_for_writer; the corvus userspace consumes the entire kernel cap-device + /srv stack). Self-audit clean — C-22 fresh-query (never caches caps); fail-closed peer_live_caps on syscall error + dead peer; bootstrap exception bounded to single-threaded corvus's TOCTOU-free count check; constant-time-per-byte passphrase compare over the equal-length window; explicit cap_mask equality (not subset) at /cap/use. **Posture**: 525/525 PASS × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. Boot test now exercises every production path of the hostowner-elevation flow end-to-end. **Reference**: new `docs/reference/76-admin-elevate.md`. **Next**: P5-hostowner-c — RECOVER verb (CORVUS-DESIGN.md §5.6); WRAP admin path; USER_DELETE; ROTATE_KEY. Couples with CRVS persistence + installer-driven first-boot setup that retires the hardcoded `SYSTEM_PASSPHRASE`. Predecessor: P5-hostowner-b-a (`e809956` / `65d911a`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-hostowner-b-a landed (substantive `e809956` / hash fixup `65d911a`) — kernel `cap` elevation device.** First of two sub-chunks of P5-hostowner-b (the hostowner-elevation feature per CORVUS-DESIGN.md §5.5/§5.5.1). New kernel Dev `devcap` (dc='k', name="cap") exposing two write-only files: `/grant` (gated on writer's `CAP_GRANT_HOSTOWNER`; records `{cap_mask, target_stripes, expiry_ns}` in a bounded pending-grant table) and `/use` (gated on writer's `PROC_FLAG_CONSOLE_ATTACHED` + matching writer-stripes; ORs `cap_mask` into `writer->caps`, consumes the grant — one-shot). Wire format: `/grant` = 16-byte frame (u64 LE cap_mask + u64 LE target_stripes); `/use` = 8-byte frame (u64 LE cap_mask). Pending table: `CAP_GRANT_MAX = 16` slots, `CAP_GRANT_EXPIRY_NS = 30s`, lazy expiry on next register; re-register for the same stripes replaces in place. `CAP_GRANTABLE = CAP_HOSTOWNER` at v1.0 (other elevation-only caps may reuse the same machinery later). Two gates in two trust domains: corvus verifies the system passphrase (kernel has no notion); kernel verifies console-attached at `/use` redemption (holds even if corvus is buggy/compromised — a compromised corvus can register grants for arbitrary stripes but only a console-attached writer can redeem; corvus elevating a network process is structurally impossible). `kernel/proc.c::exits()` calls new `cap_proc_exit_notify(p)` to drop any pending grant targeting the exiting Proc (defense in depth; stripes are fresh per Proc so a recycled pid never accidentally elevates, but cleanup frees the slot). The Dev `write` op (`devcap_write`) is a thin shim that resolves `current_thread()->proc` and dispatches to `cap_register_grant_for_writer` or `cap_redeem_grant_for_writer`; tests call the cores directly. **No spec change** — the elevation mechanism is the implementation of `specs/corvus.tla::HostownerGrant` + `HostownerRequiresConsole` and `specs/handles.tla::ElevationOnly`/`RforkStripsElevation`, all of which already model it. **Audit-bearing** per CLAUDE.md §25.4 (`kernel/devcap.c` + the `kernel/proc.c` exit hook + the syscall surface that `devcap_write` reaches through). Self-audit clean — gate enforcement at both entry points; explicit-equality matching on `/use` to avoid subset-overlap surprises; one-shot consume + grant retention on mismatch; bounded table + lazy expiry. The userspace consumer lands at P5-hostowner-b-b: corvus's `ADMIN_ELEVATE` (verb_id=7) writes `/grant`; joey's post-OK redemption writes `/use`; admin verbs (`USER_CREATE`, `USER_DELETE`, `WRAP` admin path, `ROTATE_KEY`) gate on the peer's live `caps & CAP_HOSTOWNER` via `SYS_SRV_PEER`. **Posture**: 525/525 PASS × default + UBSan (511 → 525; +14 `devcap.*` cases covering Dev registration / walk / open gating / both write-gate enforcement / table-full / one-shot consume / mismatch retention / exit cleanup). **Reference**: new `docs/reference/75-devcap.md`. **Next**: P5-hostowner-b-b. Predecessor: P5-corvus-srv-impl audit close (`232c89b` / `0510551`).
- **Older tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl audit close (substantive `232c89b` / hash fixup `0510551`) — 0 P0 / 1 P1 / 5 P2 / 4 P3 / 4 withdrawn.** Single opus prosecutor round (`a86ced547183bd486`) over the entire P5-corvus-srv-impl -a + -b arc — kernel-side `/srv` transport (devsrv + srvconn + handle + syscall + poll + proc), the userspace corvus 9P2000.L server (`usr/corvus/src/main.rs` + new `usr/corvus/src/p9.rs` codec), joey's orchestration. **F1 [P1] fixed**: the deadline-bounded handshake CORVUS-DESIGN §6.2 promises was plumbed but never engaged in production — `sys_srv_connect_for_proc` + the KOBJ_SRV arms of `sys_read_for_proc` / `sys_write_for_proc` skipped `srvconn_set_client_deadline`, leaving `client_deadline_ns = 0` which `tsleep` reads as "no deadline." A hung corvus wedged joey indefinitely. The fix adds two new `<thylacine/srvconn.h>` constants (`SRVCONN_HANDSHAKE_DEADLINE_NS = 5s` for the kernel-only Tversion+Tattach+Twalk+Tlopen path; `SRVCONN_OP_DEADLINE_NS = 30s` for steady-state ops that can stir Argon2id+AEGIS+ML-KEM on emulated targets) and the corresponding `srvconn_set_client_deadline(cn, timer_now_ns() + DEADLINE_NS)` call at every production blocking-op site. **F2 [P2] fixed**: missing `_Static_assert`s on `SrvService.magic` + `devsrv_svc_ref.magic` offsets (read by 8+ KObj_Srv discriminator consumer sites). **F3 [P2] fixed**: Q11 BadFormat did not tear down corvus's conn — the design's "stream cannot be safely re-synced across a version mismatch" was relied on the client to disconnect (the joey test passed only because joey explicitly closed). New per-Conn `tear_down_after_drain` flag set by `try_dispatch_verb` on Q11+oversize-payload paths; `service_conn` returns `Ok(false)` (closes the conn) once the BadFormat reply has been drained by the next Tread, so the client observes the error BEFORE the EOF. **F4 [P2] fixed**: corvus discarded `t_srv_peer` failure rc, stored zero-stripes peer identity in `Conn` — future admin verbs reading `caps`/`stripes` for gating would have aliased a failed read with a fail-closed-zero. Now corvus `t_close`s the just-accepted handle on non-zero `t_srv_peer` rc. **F5 [P2] fixed**: spec/impl drift — `corvus.tla::SrvBind`'s `~(\E c \in connections : c.peer = p)` precondition + append-only `connections` forbade the reconnect pattern the impl supports (joey's b3b test does exactly this: open, Q11 tear-down, reopen, fresh AUTH ok). Added a new `ConnTeardown(cn)` spec action that removes the binding from the live `connections` set; added a parallel APPEND-ONLY `connections_history` variable; `ConnOpIdentityIsKernelTruth` now checks against the history (the post-hoc invariant is "at op-time the kernel had this binding"); `SrvBind`'s peer-uniqueness stays against the live set so a Proc can reconnect after teardown. **F6 [P2] fixed**: `sys_srv_connect_handler` + `sys_post_service_handler` didn't pre-validate the user-VA range before the per-byte copy loops — inconsistent with every other syscall-surface handler. Added `sys_validate_user_buf` calls. **F9 [P3] fixed**: corvus's `pending_request` accumulator wedged at the 4320-byte cap; now clears on overflow so a subsequent well-formed Twrite can recover. **F8 / F10 / F12 [P3] documented** (no-impl-change defensive hardening at v1.0). **F7 / F11 / F13 / F14 withdrawn** (analytically sound on closer reading). **Spec posture**: all 8 `corvus_buggy_*.cfg` re-verified to still produce expected counterexamples after ConnTeardown + connections_history (3 connection-layer + 5 session-layer); the clean `corvus.cfg` partially re-verified (74M distinct states / diameter 22 / 17 min, no invariant violation) before TLC was killed — the state space grew ~3× under the F5 spec change. **Spec-to-code rule suspended for corvus** going forward (user direction); the 8 buggy cfgs remain the practical pre-commit gate. **Posture**: 511/511 PASS × default + UBSan unchanged through every fix. **Reference**: closed-list `audit_p5_corvus_srv_impl_closed_list.md` (the do-not-re-report set); `docs/reference/74-corvus-9p-server.md` Status gained an "Audit-close changes" section enumerating F1/F3/F4/F9. **Next**: P5-hostowner-b — the kernel `cap` device + `/grant` + `/use` + ADMIN_ELEVATE + admin-gated USER_CREATE/_DELETE/ROTATE_KEY; per CORVUS-DESIGN §5.5/5.5.1. - **Older tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b3b landed (substantive `565ad3e` / hash fixup `36de980`) — corvus 9P2000.L server + joey switches to /srv/corvus.** Fourth and final sub-chunk of **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b** (#524) — **THE atomic transport swap**. The pipe-pair harness (corvus's fd 0/1 + joey's `t_spawn_full` with two inherited fd-pair endpoints) is **retired**; corvus becomes a real **9P2000.L server** posting `/srv/corvus`, and joey reaches it via `t_srv_connect("corvus", "ctl")`. **Wire format + verb semantics unchanged** at the dispatch layer — the binary verb frames (CORVUS-DESIGN.md §6.4, with the 4-byte request header from b1) and all five verbs (AUTH + USER_CREATE + WRAP + UNWRAP + SESSION_CLOSE — all crypto preserved from -c / -d) flow through the new transport. **NEW: `usr/corvus/src/p9.rs`** (~370 LOC) — pure-Rust 9P2000.L codec; Tmsg parsers + Rmsg builders for the 8 ops corvus serves (Tversion / Tauth-reject / Tattach / Twalk / Tlopen / Tread / Twrite / Tclunk + Rlerror); mirrors `kernel/9p_wire.h` constants byte-for-byte. **`usr/corvus/src/main.rs`**: major I/O-layer rewrite (~770 lines diff). Per-Conn struct `{handle, peer:TSrvPeerInfo, fids[8], in_buf, out_buf, pending_request, pending_response, pending_response_off}`; `srv_server_loop(listener)` polls `[listener, conns...]` via `t_poll(-1)`, accepts new conns via `t_srv_accept + t_srv_peer`, services ready conns by draining one or more complete 9P Tmsg's per pass; `dispatch_one` parses one Tmsg + produces one Rmsg; **`/ctl` is message-oriented** — Tread IGNORES offset (drains from per-Conn `pending_response`); Twrite appends to per-Conn `pending_request` + triggers `try_dispatch_verb` once a complete verb frame is observed, which calls the verb handler, stages the response in `pending_response` (3-byte hdr + payload), and the next Tread drains it. Verb handler signatures changed from `(payload) -> Result<Vec<u8>, Status>` to `(payload: &[u8], response: &mut Vec<u8>)` (caller-owned buffer) — semantics unchanged. **`usr/joey/joey.c`**: pipe-pair replaced with `t_spawn_with_perms("corvus", no_fds=0, caps, T_SPAWN_PERM_MAY_POST_SERVICE)` + `connect_corvus()` wrapping a 60-iteration × 1000 ms-yield `t_srv_connect` retry. The retry budget accommodates corvus's 24 MiB BSS exec_setup latency on emulated QEMU AArch64 (where TCG zeroes ~4 million u64 stores across an order-13 32 MiB contiguous buddy block — easily 10+ seconds). All 9 verbs + the Q11 negative regression (verb frame with `protocol_version=99` → BadFormat + tear-down + joey reconnects + fresh AUTH ok) preserved end-to-end. **`usr/lib/libthyla-rs/src/lib.rs`**: `TSrvPeerInfo` 24-byte repr-C struct + `t_post_service / t_srv_accept / t_srv_peer / t_srv_connect` Rust wrappers. **`usr/lib/libt/include/thyla/syscall.h`**: `T_SYS_SRV_CONNECT=30` enum + `t_srv_connect` + `t_poll` C wrappers. **NEW: `usr/lib/libt/include/thyla/poll.h`**: userspace `struct pollfd` + `POLL*` ABI mirror of kernel `<thylacine/poll.h>`. **No spec change** — `corvus.tla`'s `ConnAccept` / `ConnTeardown` / `ConnOpIdentityIsKernelTruth` / `MarkMayPost` / `PostService` / `AuthSuccess` / `SessionClose` already model every transition; this is impl-against-spec. 7 fast specs re-verified clean GREEN. **Audit-bearing** per CLAUDE.md §25.4 — corvus is userspace (not directly in the trigger table) but consumes the entire kernel-side `/srv` stack (devsrv + srvconn + handle + syscall + poll, all in the trigger table); the formal P5-corvus-srv-impl audit (#525) closes after b3b. Self-audit clean — request frame accumulator bounded by msize; response staging single-flight; fid table fixed-size with explicit overflow guard; verb-handler crypto invariants preserved (C-3, AEGIS-256 nonce discipline, hybrid-PKE envelope shape). **Posture**: **511/511 PASS × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors.** The boot test IS the regression — joey's clean exit (all 9 verbs + Q11 + reconnect succeed) → `Thylacine boot OK` marker → test PASS. **Reference**: new `docs/reference/74-corvus-9p-server.md` (full as-built — architecture, /srv/corvus namespace + QIDs, pure-Rust 9P codec, per-Conn state, server loop, Tmsg dispatch, verb-handler signatures, spec↔code mapping, tests, caveats including the build-tooling trap). `docs/reference/66-corvus-server.md` Status section rewritten to point to 74. **Notable debugging lesson** (captured in 74 + `docs/phase5-status.md` Trip hazards): the previous session spent 40+ iterations chasing a "vanishing prints" mystery that was actually a build-tooling bug — `tools/build.sh disk` rebuilds the virtio-blk image but NOT the ramfs.cpio (initrd); the canonical rebuild is `tools/build.sh kernel`. With the proper rebuild, the b3b code worked first time. **Next**: P5-corvus-srv-impl audit (#525) — full multi-prosecutor round over the entire -a + -b arc. Predecessor: P5-corvus-srv-impl-b3a (`c4c8b1b` / `a2e1019`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b3a landed (substantive `c4c8b1b` / hash fixup `a2e1019`) — `SYS_SPAWN_WITH_PERMS` infrastructure (race-free spawn-time stamp of `PROC_FLAG_*` bits).** Third of four sub-chunks of **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b** (#524) — the spawn variant joey will use at b3b to grant `/sbin/corvus` `PROC_FLAG_MAY_POST_SERVICE` so corvus can call `SYS_POST_SERVICE("corvus")`. **`SYS_SPAWN_WITH_PERMS = 31`** (`name_va, name_len, fd_list_va, fd_count, cap_mask, perm_flags`) extends `SYS_SPAWN_FULL` with a sixth argument carrying `SPAWN_PERM_*` bits the kernel stamps on the spawned child atomically inside the spawn thunk, BEFORE `exec_setup` — so the child's very first user-mode instruction observes the final `proc_flags`. **The race this closes**: a post-spawn `mark(child_pid)` syscall leaves a window in which the child could reach `SYS_POST_SERVICE` before the parent's mark lands (worst case on SMP — the child runs on another CPU between spawn-return and the parent's next syscall). Baking the stamp into the spawn path itself eliminates the window structurally. **`SPAWN_PERM_MAY_POST_SERVICE`** is the v1.0 bit; granting it (or any future `SPAWN_PERM_*`) requires the calling Proc to be `PROC_FLAG_CONSOLE_ATTACHED` (the v1.0 local-console trust anchor — joey). `perm_flags = 0` is identical to `SYS_SPAWN_FULL` and doesn't require console-attach (single entry point; callers that confer no permissions don't need a separate code path). **Implementation**: `sys_spawn_full_for_proc` refactored as a thin wrapper around the new shared core `sys_spawn_full_with_perms_for_proc`; `sys_spawn_with_perms_for_proc` is the public entry that gate-checks `perm_flags` (console-attached + bits ⊆ `SPAWN_PERM_ALL`) then dispatches to the shared core. `spawn_with_fds_args` gained `u32 perm_flags`. `sys_spawn_with_fds_thunk` reads `sa->perm_flags` before `kfree(sa)`, then applies each set bit to the child Proc before the fd-install loop + `exec_setup` (the order is load-bearing — the stamp must precede any code path the child could reach; `extinction` on unknown bits at thunk time is the defense-in-depth invariant). **Userspace**: `t_spawn_with_perms` added to both libt (`<thyla/syscall.h>`) and libthyla-rs; bit mirror `T_SPAWN_PERM_MAY_POST_SERVICE`. libthyla-rs also got the `T_SYS_POST_SERVICE / _SRV_ACCEPT / _SRV_PEER / _SRV_CONNECT` constants (numbering completeness; wrappers land with b3b where corvus consumes them). **No spec change** — `corvus.tla`'s `MarkMayPost` already models PROC_FLAG_MAY_POST_SERVICE; the new syscall is one of two race-equivalent paths (kernel stamp at boot via `joey_thunk` for joey itself; spawn-thunk stamp via this syscall for joey's children) to reach the same flag, both materialized by the same kernel function `proc_mark_may_post_service`. **Tests** (4 new, `kernel/test/test_sys_spawn_with_perms.c`): `zero_perm_is_spawn_full` (perm=0 → child gets no may-post stamp, identical to SYS_SPAWN_FULL); `console_attached_grants_may_post` (kproc marked console-attached + `SPAWN_PERM_MAY_POST_SERVICE` → positive pid; child does NOT inherit console-attached, since rfork strips it and the thunk only applies the requested perms); `rejects_non_console_attached_parent` (fresh un-attached Proc as parent → -1); `rejects_unknown_perm_bits` (high garbage bit → -1, even from a console-attached parent). **Posture**: 507 → 511 PASS × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Audit-bearing**: `kernel/syscall.c` (the entire syscall surface is in the trigger table per CLAUDE.md §25.4); self-audit clean — every code path through the new entry validates `perm_flags` BEFORE any user-VA reads; the bit-ladder in the thunk fail-closes on unknown bits via `extinction`; existing SYS_SPAWN_FULL behavior preserved by the wrapper. The formal P5-corvus-srv-impl audit is **#525**, after b3b + b4. **Reference**: new `docs/reference/73-sys-spawn-with-perms.md` (full as-built — ABI, mechanism rationale, console-attachment gate, implementation, tests). **Process model**: `docs/reference/14-process-model.md` gained a new "Service-post authority" section documenting `PROC_FLAG_MAY_POST_SERVICE` + the spawn-time stamp pattern. **CORVUS-DESIGN §6.1** clarified — the joey-stamp mechanism is now named explicitly (`SYS_SPAWN_WITH_PERMS`) rather than left abstract. **Next**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b3b** (#543) — corvus userspace becomes a real 9P2000.L server. corvus's main loop replaces `read_exact(RX_FD)` → `t_poll([listener, conn_0, ..., conn_N])` → `t_srv_accept` on listener / one 9P Tmsg per ready connection. joey switches from the pipe-pair harness to `t_spawn_with_perms("corvus", ..., T_SPAWN_PERM_MAY_POST_SERVICE)` + `t_srv_connect("corvus", "ctl")`. Predecessor: P5-corvus-srv-impl-b2 (`4dc0f75` / `2af526e`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b2 landed (substantive `4dc0f75` / hash fixup `2af526e`) — kernel `SYS_SRV_CONNECT` + KObj_Srv r/w dispatch + per-Proc one-connection cap + handshake drive.** Second of four sub-chunks of **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b** — the kernel-side machinery a client needs to reach a `/srv/<svc>` server. **`struct Proc`** gains `u8 srv_conn_count` (replaces `_pad_flags` — `sizeof(struct Proc)` stays 144). **`struct SrvConn`** gains `u32 client_fid` + `bool client_handshake_done` + `u64 client_offset` — set by the handshake drive on the open path, read by the r/w dispatch. **`srvconn_drive_client_handshake(cn, peer_pid, path, path_len)`** (`kernel/srvconn.c`) composes `p9_client_handshake` (Tversion + Tattach with `uname = "thylacine"`, `n_uname = peer_pid`) with an optional `p9_client_walk_one(root_fid → fid 2, [path])` + `p9_client_lopen(fid 2, O_RDWR)` (Linux flags directly, mirroring `dev9p_open`); on success `cn->client_fid` is set, `client_handshake_done = true`. Each blocking recv is `tsleep`-bounded by the caller's `srvconn_set_client_deadline` — a hung corvus times out. **`srvconn_client_read` / `srvconn_client_write`** wrap `p9_client_read` / `p9_client_write` on `cn->client_fid` with `cn->client_offset` (advanced on the byte count actually transferred — mirrors `Spoor.offset` in `dev9p_read/write`). Both gate on `handshake_done` + `srvconn_is_live(cn)` — pre-handshake or post-teardown calls fail-close (-1). **`SYS_SRV_CONNECT = 30`** (`name_va, name_len, path_va, path_len`) composes `srv_conn_open_for_proc` with `srvconn_drive_client_handshake`; on handshake failure the just-installed handle is closed (which teardown + unref's the SrvConn AND decrements the per-Proc count). **Per-Proc-one-connection cap** (`SRV_CONN_PER_PROC_MAX = 1`) is checked at the top of `srv_conn_open_for_proc` (fail-fast — no allocation burned on the rejected attempt); incremented after the handle install (where the SrvConn is committed); decremented in `handle_close`'s KOBJ_SRV `SRV_CONN_MAGIC` arm BEFORE `handle_release_obj` (which can clobber the SrvConn's magic via `srvconn_unref`'s last-ref free). proc_free's bulk-close path (which goes directly to `handle_release_obj`, no Proc) bypasses the decrement, which is fine — the Proc is being torn down. **KOBJ_SRV r/w dispatch**: new `sys_lookup_rw_handle` helper validates an r/w-capable handle (KOBJ_SPOOR or KOBJ_SRV with `SRV_CONN_MAGIC`); `sys_read_for_proc` / `sys_write_for_proc` switch on `slot->kind` — KOBJ_SPOOR routes the existing Spoor.dev->read/write path, KOBJ_SRV routes `srvconn_client_read/write`. The zero-length-r/w validation shortcuts in the handlers also go through `sys_lookup_rw_handle` so a zero-byte op on a KObj_Srv handle correctly validates the handle without faulting. **6 new tests** (`test_srv_client.c`): `srv_client.{per_proc_cap_blocks_second_open, handle_close_decrements_cap, read_write_fail_pre_handshake, handshake_times_out_without_responder, sys_srv_connect_unknown_service, sys_srv_connect_per_proc_cap}` — covering the cap (in both `srv_conn_open_for_proc` and `SYS_SRV_CONNECT`), the close-then-reopen decrement, the pre-handshake gate, the deadline-fired-without-responder timeout path (no synthetic responder needed here; the full handshake-success path lands in b3 against the real corvus 9P server). **No spec change** — `corvus.tla` connection layer already models `ClientConnect` / `ClientOp`; this is impl-against-spec. Every spec module byte-unchanged. 5 fast specs re-verified clean GREEN. **Posture**: 501 → 507 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Audit-bearing** per CLAUDE.md §25.4 (`kernel/srvconn.c` + `kernel/devsrv.c` + `kernel/handle.c` + `kernel/syscall.c` — all in trigger table). Self-audit clean. **Reference**: `docs/reference/71-srvconn.md` Status table + Known caveats expanded for b2. **Next**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b3** — corvus becomes a real 9P2000.L server (Tversion / Tauth-reject / Tattach / Twalk / Tlopen / Tread / Twrite / Tclunk) over its accepted connections; the b2 handshake drive is exercised end-to-end against the real consumer. Predecessor: P5-corvus-srv-impl-b1 (`0e7d6b1` / `4bf689c`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b1 landed (substantive `0e7d6b1` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — Q11 corvus wire 3→4 byte request header.** First of four sub-chunks of **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b** (#524) — moves corvus's request decoder + joey's encoder from a 3-byte header (`verb_id u8 + payload_len u16 LE`) to the 4-byte header `(verb_id u8 + protocol_version u8 + payload_len u16 LE)` per CORVUS-DESIGN §6.4 + STRATUM-API-V1.md Q11. **The hard gate on live corvus↔stratumd FS interop** — Stratum's UNWRAP / WRAP encoders already emit `protocol_version = 1`; corvus's decoder had to follow. **corvus** (`usr/corvus/src/main.rs`): new `const CORVUS_PROTOCOL_VERSION: u8 = 1`; `server_loop`'s header `[u8; 3]` → `[u8; 4]`; decodes `verb_id = header[0]`, `protocol_version = header[1]`, `payload_len = u16 LE from header[2..4]`; an unknown `protocol_version` is `BadFormat + terminate` (the frame's shape may differ across versions, so the stream cannot be safely re-synced — the same discipline as `payload_len > MAX_PAYLOAD_LEN`). **joey** (`usr/joey/joey.c::corvus_exchange`): `hdr[3]` → `hdr[4]`; emits `{verb, 1, payload_len & 0xff, payload_len >> 8}`. **Response frames stay 3-byte** (no version byte per §6.4). The full joey↔corvus exchange — USER_CREATE michael / susan + AUTH-wrong (BadAuth) + AUTH-ok (33-byte token) + WRAP users/michael + UNWRAP users/michael (DEK round-trip) + UNWRAP users/susan (C-7 PermissionDenied) + UNWRAP users/ghost (NotFound) + UNWRAP wrong key_id (InternalError — key_id AAD bind) + UNWRAP malformed envelope (BadFormat) + SESSION_CLOSE — passes end-to-end on the new wire. **No new tests** — the existing joey suite exercises the new wire positively; the explicit BadFormat-on-bad-version negative case lands at -b3 (corvus's multi-connection server can hot-reset; the v1.0-d single-peer harness cannot survive a deliberate desync). **Not audit-bearing** — wire format only, no kernel surface change. **No spec change** — every spec module byte-unchanged. **Posture**: 501/501 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Reference**: `docs/reference/66-corvus-server.md` Request-frame block + server-loop pseudocode updated for the 4-byte header. **Next**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b2** — kernel-side production client-open syscall routing namespace `open("/srv/<name>/...")` into `srv_conn_open_for_proc` with the §6.2 step-5 handshake drive (Tversion + Tattach + Twalk + Topen on the SrvConn's kernel-owned `p9_client`); the per-Proc-one-connection cap; KOBJ_SRV read/write dispatch (similar to P5-poll-b's parallel-handle-kind dispatch) translating SYS_READ/WRITE on a client connection handle into Tread/Twrite over the SrvConn; the joey post-gate-stamp mechanism. Predecessor: P5-poll audit close (`997134f` / `a7ad07c`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-poll audit close (substantive `997134f` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — 0 P0 / 2 P1 / 2 P2 / 7 P3, all addressed.** Single opus prosecutor round over the complete P5-poll surface — `kernel/poll.c` (mechanism), both `.poll` implementors (`devpipe` at P5-poll-a + `devsrv` at P5-poll-b via `srvconn_poll` + `svc_listener_poll` + `srv_handle_poll`), every readiness mutation site, the user-VA wrapper, and the spec ↔ impl mapping. **F1 [P2] fixed** — `srv_handle_poll`'s `SRV_CONN_MAGIC` arm was delegating to `srvconn_poll` (server-endpoint revents) on a client-side KObj_Srv handle; the header comment already declared "fail-closed POLLNVAL until the client connection poll story lands" but the impl contradicted; arm now returns POLLNVAL. **F2 [P2] fixed** — `srvconn_teardown` latched `c2s.eof` then `s2c.eof` under SEPARATE locks; a mid-teardown poll (which acquires both channel locks together) could observe POLLHUP without POLLERR. Teardown now takes both channel locks in the fixed `c2s → s2c` order (same as `srvconn_poll`, no new deadlock), sets both EOFs inside the dual-lock critical section, then wakes. **F3 [P1] doc-fixed** — `<thylacine/poll.h>` preamble gained a "HANDLE-SLOT LIFETIME (v1.0 INVARIANT)" section declaring that poll's borrowed-handle-slot soundness depends on single-thread-per-Proc; multi-thread-per-Proc lift must bump per-kobj-kind refcounts at poll entry and drop at the unregister sweep. **F4 [P1] fixed** — `poll_scan_one`'s KOBJ_SPOOR branch treated NULL-obj as "always-ready" (inconsistent with KOBJ_SRV NULL-obj → POLLNVAL); now `!sp \|\| !sp->dev` → POLLNVAL (malformed handle), keeping the legitimate "Dev with NULL `.poll`" → always-ready path for the POSIX-regular-file case. **P3 fixes** (F5/F7/F10/F11): documented `poll_total_slept`'s "slow-path entered, not necessarily parked" semantic; commented the unregister-then-magic-scrub ordering as load-bearing; expanded poll.h's lock chain to the full `object → list → g_timerwait → rendez → cpu_sched`; removed `srvconn_server_send`'s unnecessary `poll_waiter_list_wake` (with F1's fix, no client-side poll exists; the wake reached no poller — restored at the future client-side poll path). **F6/F8 withdrawn no-change** — F6 (re-scan POLLNVAL re-counting) is dead-code-safe (the fast path fires); F8 (spec's monotonic-readiness vs impl retraction) is POSIX-acceptable retraction the spec deliberately abstracts. **F9 partial** — 4 new regression / coverage tests: `poll.null_obj_spoor_pollnval` (F4 regression), `poll.client_srv_handle_pollnval` (F1 regression), `poll.mixed_spoor_and_srv` (cross-kobj-kind dispatch), `poll.max_nfds` (nfds = PROC_HANDLE_MAX = 64 boundary — exercises the 2 KiB `waiters[]` stack allocation). **Posture**: 497 → 501 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **No spec change** — `poll.tla` byte-unchanged; 5 fast specs re-verified clean GREEN + 3 poll buggy cfgs counterexample. **Audit closed-list**: `memory/audit_p5_poll_closed_list.md`. **Next**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b** (#524) — corvus becomes a real 9P2000.L server reading bytes off `/srv/corvus` connection Spoors, multiplexing them via `SYS_POLL` against its listener (the consumer the entire P5-poll arc was built for). Predecessor: P5-poll-b (`9fdcf08` / `35f10f9`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-poll-b landed (substantive `9fdcf08` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — `devsrv` poll: the connection-Spoor endpoint + the `KObj_Srv` listener.** Third sub-chunk of **P5-poll**, the multi-fd wait primitive (ARCH §23.3); closes the mechanism's v1.0 surface (the formal P5-poll audit #538 runs next, over `kernel/poll.c` + both `.poll` implementors + every readiness site). Two new pollable surfaces, both implementing `specs/poll.tla`'s `Register` + `MakeReady` actions directly. **The connection Spoor** (the `KObj_Spoor` handle corvus gets from `SYS_SRV_ACCEPT`): `devsrv_poll` (the Dev vtable slot) dispatches by aux — `/srv` root + service-ref Spoors return 0 (not pollable as transport); connection Spoor → delegates to **`srvconn_poll`** (`kernel/srvconn.c`). `srvconn_poll` is atomic register-then-observe under both channel locks taken in a fixed order (c2s → s2c — no other path takes both, so the dual-lock acquire is safe): POLLIN ↔ `c2s.count > 0`, POLLHUP ↔ `c2s.eof`, POLLOUT ↔ `!s2c.eof && s2c.count < SRVCONN_RING_CAP`, POLLERR ↔ `s2c.eof`. `struct SrvConn` gained ONE `poll_waiter_list poll_list` covering both directions (the polled object IS the connection — every readiness edge is a single wake of every registered poller). Wake callouts at every readiness mutation: `srvconn_client_send` (after `chan_produce` on c2s — POLLIN edge), `srvconn_server_send` (s2c), `srvconn_teardown` (after both `chan_set_eof`s — POLLHUP + POLLERR latch simultaneously). **The listener** (the `KObj_Srv` handle `SYS_POST_SERVICE` returned — corvus polls it to learn when a client has connected): the KObj_Srv handle kind is NOT a Spoor — the Dev `.poll` vtable can't reach it. `kernel/poll.c::poll_scan_one` was refactored to switch on handle kind — KOBJ_SPOOR → existing `dev->poll` path; KOBJ_SRV → new **`srv_handle_poll`** (`kernel/devsrv.c`, declared in `<thylacine/devsrv.h>`); default → POLLNVAL. `srv_handle_poll` reads the obj's first u64 (its magic) and routes to `svc_listener_poll` (SrvService — the listener) or `srvconn_poll` (SrvConn — exposed for forward-compat); unknown magic → POLLNVAL. **`svc_listener_poll`** samples + registers atomically under `g_srv_registry.lock`: POLLIN ↔ `backlog_count > 0`, POLLHUP ↔ `state != LIVE`. `struct SrvService` gained a `poll_waiter_list poll_list`, initialized in `devsrv_init` alongside the SRV_SERVICE_MAGIC stamp. Listener wake callouts at `srv_conn_open_for_proc` (the push — backlog grew), `srv_proc_exit_notify` (the tombstone — POLLHUP edge), `srv_registry_reset` (test-only drain). Every wake fires AFTER its outer lock is released — the lock chain is acyclic: registry → poll_list → rendez (for the listener); c2s → s2c → poll_list → rendez (for the connection). **No spec change** — `poll.tla` byte-unchanged; the two new `.poll` implementors instantiate the same `Register` + `MakeReady` actions the spec already models; `poll.tla` clean GREEN (3 cfgs) + 3 buggy counterexample, 7 fast specs re-verified clean (handles.tla byte-unchanged — skipped per the 65-min discipline). **Tests** (8 new, in `kernel/test/test_poll.c`): `poll.devsrv_listener_{immediate_pollin,empty_not_ready,block_then_wake,pollhup_on_tombstone}` (the listener surface) + `poll.devsrv_conn_{pollin_on_send,pollout_immediate,pollhup_on_teardown,block_then_wake_pollin}` (the connection surface) — covers fast/slow paths, teardown propagation, dual-thread block-then-wake. **Posture**: 489 → 497 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Audit**: `kernel/poll.c` + `kernel/devsrv.c` + `kernel/srvconn.c` all audit-bearing per CLAUDE.md §25.4 (consolidated under existing trigger-table rows); self-audit clean across the CLAUDE.md hazard categories — lock ordering (object → list → rendez, no inversion), hook lifetime (the existing sweep covers KOBJ_SRV pollers too — the unregister sweep walks every `waiters[i]` regardless of which Dev/object the hook is on), error-path cleanups (every exit goes through the sweep label), boundary conditions, spec-action mapping (`SPEC-TO-CODE.md` poll.tla section extended with devsrv refs); the formal P5-poll audit is **#538**. **Reference**: `docs/reference/72-poll.md` Status + Error paths + Tests sections updated for the second implementor; `70-devsrv.md` gained a new "poll" section + a Status row; `71-srvconn.md` gained a new "poll" section + a Status row. User-manual not touched (`docs/manual/05-syscalls.md` planned but does not exist). `specs/SPEC-TO-CODE.md` poll.tla section's `MakeReady(f)` row extended with the new devsrv/srvconn file refs. **Next**: the P5-poll audit (#538), then **P5-corvus-srv-impl-b** (#524) — corvus becomes a real 9P2000.L server reading bytes off `/srv/corvus` connection Spoors, multiplexing them via `SYS_POLL` against its listener. Predecessor: P5-poll-a (`4ef1537` / `d8518af`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-poll-a landed (substantive `4ef1537` / hash fixup `d8518af`) — the kernel `poll` mechanism + `SYS_POLL` (syscall 29) + `devpipe` poll + the `t_poll` libt stub.** Second sub-chunk of **P5-poll**, the multi-fd wait primitive (ARCH §23.3; gate-tied Phase-5 spec #6). Implements `specs/poll.tla` directly: a poller waits on N fds whose readiness lives behind N different locks, sleeping on its **own private `Rendez`** via `tsleep` (preserving the single-waiter discipline) and registering a `poll_waiter` hook on each polled object's hook list. **`struct poll_waiter`** (`<thylacine/poll.h>`): stack-allocated per pollfd, `nfds ≤ PROC_HANDLE_MAX = 64` → a `waiters[64]` array on the kernel stack; `magic`/`ready`/`rendez`/`list`/`next` fields; `list` back-pointer is what lets the unregister sweep find each hook's home without a Dev vtable op. **`struct poll_waiter_list`** owns its **own** spin_lock (separate from the polled object's lock): lock order globally is **object → list → rendez**; unregister takes only the list lock so it cannot deadlock with a concurrent producer holding the object lock. **`Dev.poll`** vtable slot added to `<thylacine/dev.h>` between `bwrite` and `remove` (designated initializers in all 10 Devs make placement safe). The slot's contract: pw!=NULL registers + samples atomically under the object's lock — the load-bearing **register-then-observe** step; pw==NULL is sample-only; NULL slot ⇒ always-ready. **`devpipe_poll`** (`kernel/pipe.c`) is the v1.0 implementor: read end gets POLLIN on `count > 0` + POLLHUP on `write_eof`; write end gets POLLOUT on `count < BUF_SIZE && !read_eof` + POLLERR on `read_eof`. Every existing wakeup site in pipe.c (close × 2 paths, read drain, write append) gains a **`poll_waiter_list_wake`** callout: walks under the list lock, sets each `pw->ready=true` BEFORE calling `wakeup(pw->rendez)` — the order is load-bearing (the rendez-lock release/acquire pair carries the `ready` write across to the poller's cond re-check). `struct pipe_ring` header grew 72 → 88 B (16 B for the new `poll_list`); `_Static_assert` re-pinned. **`kernel/poll.c`**: `sys_poll_for_proc` (testable core; ~80 lines) — validate args, stack-alloc waiters + private Rendez, first scan via `dev->poll(c, events, &waiters[i])`, fast-path return if `ready_count > 0` or `timeout_ms == 0`, else `tsleep` with deadline from `timer_now_ns() + ms*1e6` (clamp on u64 wrap; 0→1 to avoid the "no deadline" sentinel), post-wake re-scan via `dev->poll(c, events, NULL)`, **unregister sweep** + `pw->magic = 0` scrub at every exit. **`sys_poll_handler`** wraps user-VA: copies the full pollfd[] in (so fd+events are read once before any sleep), writes back ONLY the 2-byte revents per pollfd with per-byte fault fixup; partial-write fault scrubs already-written revents to 0 (the `sys_srv_peer_handler` torn-write defence). **`SYS_POLL = 29`** added to `<thylacine/syscall.h>`; dispatch case in `kernel/syscall.c`. **libt stub**: `t_poll` + `TPollFd` + `T_POLL{IN,OUT,ERR,HUP,NVAL}` constants in `usr/lib/libthyla-rs/src/lib.rs` — the corvus-side consumer at P5-corvus-srv-impl-b. **Tests** (12, all PASS): `poll.{ready_immediately_{pollin,pollout},timeout_{zero_not_ready,positive_fires},block_then_wake_pollin,pollhup_on_close_write_end,multi_fd_one_ready,bad_fd_revents_pollnval,bad_args_rejected,always_ready_null_dev_poll,pollerr_on_write_after_read_close,unregister_after_fast_path}` — covers both fast and slow paths, multi-fd, POLLNVAL/POLLHUP/POLLERR, NULL-`.poll` always-ready (via devnull), and the regression case of fast-path properly unregistering hooks. **No spec change** — implements directly against `specs/poll.tla`'s `Register`/`CommitOrSleep`/`MakeReady`/`NoStaleHook`; `poll.tla` clean GREEN (3 cfgs) + 3 buggy counterexample, the 9 other spec modules byte-unchanged. **Posture**: 477 → 489 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Audit**: `kernel/poll.c` is audit-bearing per CLAUDE.md §25.4; self-audit clean (lock ordering, hook lifetime, error-path cleanups, boundary conditions); the formal P5-poll audit closes at #538 after P5-poll-b. **Reference**: new `docs/reference/72-poll.md` (the full as-built — public API, register-then-observe, lock ordering, state machines, spec mapping, error paths). User-manual not touched — `docs/manual/05-syscalls.md` is planned but doesn't exist yet; the syscall-reference touch is owed when that page lands. `specs/SPEC-TO-CODE.md` poll.tla section filled with file:line refs. **Next**: P5-poll-b (`devsrv` connection + listener `.poll`). Predecessor: P5-poll-spec (`891f9d2` / `d0926c6`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-poll-spec landed (substantive `891f9d2` / hash fixup `d0926c6`) — `specs/poll.tla` + the `SYS_POLL` scripture pins (spec + scripture; no code).** First sub-chunk of **P5-poll**, the multi-fd wait primitive (ARCH §23.3; the gate-tied Phase-5 spec #6) — a prerequisite of P5-corvus-srv-impl-b, since corvus is single-threaded and `poll`s its `/srv/corvus` listener plus its accepted connections, and Thylacine has no other kernel "wait on N sources" primitive (the user-signed-off Model 3; Plan-9-pure proc-per-connection corvus is the documented v1.x evolution). **Spec** (spec-first, before any impl): new `specs/poll.tla` models one poller waiting on N fds whose readiness lives behind N different locks — the poller sleeps on its **own private `Rendez`** via `tsleep` (preserving the single-waiter `Rendez` discipline) and registers a lightweight `poll_waiter` hook on each polled object's hook list; the load-bearing **register-then-observe** discipline (`dev->poll` installs the hook and samples readiness in one locked step) closes the missed-wakeup race across N fds. Predecessor: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3c (`56b4a6f` / `8f46d20`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3c landed (substantive `56b4a6f` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — `SYS_SRV_PEER`, corvus's read of a `/srv` connection's kernel-stamped peer identity.** Third and final sub-chunk of the P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3 per-connection layer (CORVUS-DESIGN §6.3; invariant C-22) — with it **a3 is complete and P5-corvus-srv-impl-a, the kernel side of the `/srv/corvus` transport, is closed**. **`SYS_SRV_PEER`** (syscall 28; testable core `sys_srv_peer_for_proc`, user-VA wrapper `sys_srv_peer_handler`): given a `KObj_Spoor` connection endpoint handle it writes a 24-byte `struct srv_peer_info` `{ stripes, caps, console, alive }` to a user-VA buffer — the kernel's unforgeable answer to "who is on the other end," which corvus reads per request and never caches on its fid state. **Immutable identity** (`stripes`, the console bit) comes straight off the `SrvConn`, captured by value at mint — knowable even after the peer exits, no Proc lookup, no UAF. **Live caps** come from new **`proc_caps_by_stripes`** (`kernel/proc.c`): a scan of the process table under `g_proc_table_lock` (via `proc_for_each`) for an `ALIVE` Proc carrying `stripes`, snapshotting its `caps` by value — the **dead-Proc guard**: a zombie / reaped peer has no `ALIVE` match, so `caps` and `alive` fail-close to `0`, never a stale snapshot (the kernel half of `corvus.tla` `ConnOpPeerWasLive`); only the caps value escapes the lock, never a Proc pointer. **Poster gate**: the `SrvConn` gained a `server_stripes` field — the poster's `stripes`, captured by value at mint (`srvconn_create`'s new 4th parameter; `srv_conn_open_for_proc` reads `poster_stripes` under the registry lock) — and `SYS_SRV_PEER` refuses any caller whose `stripes` ≠ `server_stripes`, so only the service poster (corvus) may query its connections' peers. `struct srv_peer_info` is a syscall-ABI type — layout pinned by `_Static_assert`s on size (24) and every field offset. `devsrv_conn_of` is now non-static (declared in `devsrv.h`) so `SYS_SRV_PEER` can resolve an endpoint handle to its `SrvConn`; three fail-closed `SrvConn` accessors added — `srvconn_peer_stripes` / `srvconn_peer_console` / `srvconn_server_stripes`. **No spec change** — `corvus.tla` `SrvPeerOp` + the invariants `ConnOpIdentityIsKernelTruth` / `ConnOpPeerWasLive` already model `SYS_SRV_PEER` (landed at P5-corvus-srv-design); this implements against them, every spec module byte-unchanged + re-verified TLC-clean. **Tests**: `kernel/test/test_devsrv_conn.c` — `devsrv.srv_peer_{identity,dead_peer,gate,bad_args}`; 473 → 477 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Self-audit clean** across the CLAUDE.md hazard categories; the formal P5-corvus-srv-impl audit is task #525, after -impl-b. **References**: `docs/reference/70-devsrv.md` (the `SYS_SRV_PEER` section + `struct srv_peer_info`), `71-srvconn.md` (`server_stripes` + accessors), `14-process-model.md` (`proc_caps_by_stripes`). **Next**: P5-corvus-srv-impl-b (corvus becomes a real 9P2000.L server over `/srv/corvus`). Predecessor: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3b (`e5ad6c6` / `16e9f9e`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3b landed (substantive `e5ad6c6` / hash fixup `16e9f9e`) — the `/srv` per-connection layer: `devsrv` walk + the accept backlog + `SYS_SRV_ACCEPT` + connection I/O + teardown.** Second of three sub-chunks of the P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3 per-connection layer (CORVUS-DESIGN §6.2). `struct SrvService` gains a **bounded FIFO accept backlog** (`SRV_ACCEPT_BACKLOG` = 16; past it a client open fails fast) plus an `accept_rendez`. **`srv_conn_open_for_proc`** is the client-connect core: it mints a `SrvConn` (a3a), enqueues it on the service's accept backlog, installs a non-transferable **`KObj_Srv`** connection handle (obj = the `SrvConn` directly) in the client's handle table, and wakes a blocked accepter; a global cap `SRV_MAX_CONNS` = 64 bounds live connections. **`SYS_SRV_ACCEPT`** (syscall 27; testable core `sys_srv_accept_for_proc`) is the poster's accept — it **blocks** (`sleep` on `accept_rendez`) until a client opens, then hands corvus the server endpoint as a **`KObj_Spoor`** `devsrv` connection Spoor; `devsrv_read` / `devsrv_write` / `devsrv_close` route that Spoor to `srvconn_server_recv` / `srvconn_server_send` / `srvconn_teardown` + `srvconn_unref` — so corvus does byte I/O with the existing `SYS_READ` / `SYS_WRITE` / `SYS_CLOSE`. The **handle-kind asymmetry is deliberate**: the client side is the peer-identity-bearing connection that must not be transferable (`KObj_Srv`, `handle_dup`-rejected); corvus's side is a server I/O endpoint, a byte-I/O Spoor. **`devsrv_walk`** is real (a `/srv` root walk one component deep yields a service Spoor); **`devsrv_open` stays a documented stub** — the client connection handle is `KObj_Srv` over a `SrvConn`, not a Spoor, so the Spoor-returning Dev `open` vtable structurally cannot host the client-connect (the production client-open syscall lands at -impl-b). **`handle_release_obj` `KOBJ_SRV`** now discriminates a service object (`SRV_SERVICE_MAGIC` → no-op) from a connection object (`SRV_CONN_MAGIC` → `srvconn_teardown` + `srvconn_unref`) by the first `u64`; `SrvService.magic` became a **permanent struct type tag** stamped once by `devsrv_init` (never cleared — a `KObj_Srv` service handle can outlive its entry's `LIVE` state and the release path must still read the magic). **`srv_proc_exit_notify`** is extended to drain a dead poster's accept backlog (each pending `SrvConn` torn down — a client blocked on a dead server wakes with EOF). **No spec change** — `corvus.tla` (`SrvBind` / `SrvAccept` / `ProcExit`) and `handles.tla` (`WalkDerive` / `WalkChildIsSrv` / `SrvHandlesAtOrigin`) already model the connection layer; every spec module byte-unchanged. **Deferred to P5-corvus-srv-impl-b** (tracked split, not a gap): the §6.2 step-5 9P handshake drive (needs a real corvus 9P server), the production client-open syscall + the `/srv` mount into a Territory, and the per-Proc-one-connection cap (a3b's DoS bounds are the per-service backlog + the global `SRV_MAX_CONNS` cap). **Tests**: `kernel/test/test_devsrv_conn.c` — `devsrv.{walk_service,conn_open,accept_immediate,accept_blocks_then_wakes,conn_io,conn_release,poster_exit_drains_backlog}`; 466 → 473 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Self-audit clean**; the formal P5-corvus-srv-impl audit is task #525, after -impl-b. **References**: `docs/reference/70-devsrv.md` extended to a3b; `71-srvconn.md` xref. **Next**: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3c (`SYS_SRV_PEER`). Predecessor: P5-kernel-l3-4mib (`079d754` / `*(pending)*`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-kernel-l3-4mib landed (substantive `079d754` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — the kernel-image L3 mapping extended 2 MiB → 4 MiB.** A focused architectural enabler, landed *before* P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3b so that chunk lands UBSan-green. The UBSan-instrumented kernel image grew past the 1.5 MiB usable ceiling of the single 2 MiB L3-block kernel mapping (image + the 512 KiB firmware reservation > 2 MiB → `ld.lld` ASSERT failure). `build_page_tables` (`arch/arm64/mmu.c`) now maps the kernel image page-grained across a **4 MiB region** built from **two contiguous L3 tables** — `l3_kernel` and `l3_directmap_kernel` are each declared `[ENTRIES_PER_TABLE * 2]` (1024 entries; the two page-aligned halves are each used as an L3 table); the TTBR0 identity, TTBR1 high-half, and direct-map alias each wire **two consecutive 2 MiB L2 entries** (one per L3-table half). The **KASLR slide is now 4 MiB-aligned** (`KASLR_ALIGN_BITS` 21 → 22, `KASLR_OFFSET_MASK` `0x3FFE00000` → `0x3FFC00000`) so the kernel's 4 MiB region never straddles a 1 GiB (L2-table) boundary — its two 2 MiB L2 entries are always consecutive in one `l2_ttbr1` table, eliminating any boot-time straddle special-case; a `_Static_assert(KASLR_ALIGN_BITS >= 22)` in `mmu.c` pins the dependency. KASLR entropy is 13 → 12 bits (8192 → 4096 distinct 4-MiB-aligned slide positions over a 16 GiB window; invariant **I-16** still holds — strong randomization). `kernel.ld`'s image ASSERT widened from `< 0x200000` to `< 0x400000` — the cap rises 1.5 MiB → **3.5 MiB**; the UBSan image is ~1.51 MiB, leaving ~2 MiB of headroom for the rest of Phase 5. **No spec change** — page-table layout is static configuration, not a §28 concurrency invariant; every spec module byte-unchanged. **Tests**: no new unit test — the UBSan-matrix boot (the image now spills into the second L3 table) exercises the new mapping end-to-end; 473/473 PASS × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Self-audit clean** (boot/MMU surface — table-array bounds vs. the `kernel.ld` ASSERT, L2 wiring, KASLR alignment). **Audit** (opus prosecutor, MMU/KASLR — close `7a6fbbe`): 0 P0 / 1 P1 / 0 P2 / 2 P3, all fixed — F1 (the TTBR0-identity + direct-map `idx + 1` L2 wiring lacked the TTBR1 path's 1 GiB-straddle guard) fixed by a new `kernel.ld` ASSERT pinning the 4 MiB region within one 1 GiB L2 table (the link-time analogue of TTBR1's runtime guard); F2/F3 comment-rot fixed. The prosecutor verified the array-bound coupling, KASLR alignment, and W^X across both L3-table halves sound. Flagged pre-existing + out-of-scope: a cache-maintenance gap (no `dc cvac/cvau` in `arch/arm64/`). Closed-list `audit_p5_kernel_l3_4mib_closed_list.md`. Scripture: `ARCHITECTURE.md §6.2` + `docs/reference/03-mmu.md` + `05-kaslr.md` updated. **Next**: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3b. Predecessor: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3a (`0cd17e6` / `*(pending)*`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3a landed (substantive `0cd17e6` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — the `SrvConn` per-connection `/srv` transport.** First of three sub-chunks of the P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3 per-connection layer (CORVUS-DESIGN §6.2 + §6.3). A **`SrvConn`** (`kernel/srvconn.c`) is one kernel-minted `/srv` connection — a bidirectional byte transport plus the opening client Proc's kernel-stamped peer identity (`stripes`, console bit, pid) captured **by value** at mint (no raw `Proc*`, so a reaped peer is no UAF). The transport is two rings: `c2s` (kernel 9P client → corvus) and `s2c` (corvus → kernel client). Each ring is sized ≥ msize and the kernel 9P client is synchronous / single-frame-in-flight, so a **writer never blocks**; the one blocking wait — the client draining `s2c` — is **`tsleep`-bounded** (CORVUS-DESIGN §6.2): a corvus that *hangs* times the client out (never wedges it), a corvus that *crashes* wakes it at once via teardown's EOF. The `SrvConn` owns a dedicated synchronous kernel `p9_client` (kernel-owned, never in a handle table — invariant C-23), initialized at mint and handshake-driven by the open path (a3b). **`srvconn_teardown`** (idempotent) flips `LIVE → TORN`, latches EOF on both rings, wakes the blocked consumer; the last `srvconn_unref` destroys the `p9_client` and frees. **No spec change** — the transport is plumbing: the `s2c` blocking drain composes `specs/tsleep.tla` / `specs/scheduler.tla` `NoMissedWakeup`, teardown's EOF-then-wake mirrors `specs/pipe.tla` `CloseWrite`; `corvus.tla`'s `SrvBind` / `SrvAccept` / `SrvPeerOp` model a level above (a3b / a3c). **Tests**: `test_srvconn.c` — `srvconn.{create_destroy,roundtrip,ring_capacity,recv_blocks_then_wakes,recv_deadline_timeout,teardown_eofs,teardown_wakes_blocked}`; 459 → 466 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Self-audit clean** across the CLAUDE.md hazard categories; the formal P5-corvus-srv-impl audit is task #525, after -impl-b. **Reference**: new `docs/reference/71-srvconn.md`. **Next**: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3b (the `devsrv` walk/open path that mints a `SrvConn`, the bounded accept queue, `SYS_SRV_ACCEPT`, the `KObj_Srv` connection-Spoor install). Predecessor: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a2 (`8d675ed` / `ece0837`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-a2 landed (substantive `8d675ed` / hash fixup `ece0837`) — the `devsrv` Dev + the `/srv` service registry + `SYS_POST_SERVICE`, the kernel surface a userspace 9P server posts itself on.** Second sub-chunk of P5-corvus-srv-impl-a (CORVUS-DESIGN §6.1; ARCH §9.4 / §11.2c). **`devsrv`** (`kernel/devsrv.c`; dc=`'s'`, Plan 9 `#s`; registered by `dev_init`) — a kernel `Dev` distinct from `dev9p` so a `/srv` Spoor is structurally a `KObj_Srv` object; at a2 only `attach` (the `/srv` root QTDIR Spoor) is meaningful, the other 15 vtable slots are graceful-fail stubs. **Service registry** (static `g_srv_registry`, `SRV_MAX_SERVICES`=8): named services keyed to their poster Proc by `stripes` *by value* (no raw `Proc*` — a reaped poster is no UAF, §6.3); slot state machine `FREE → RESERVING → LIVE → TOMBSTONED`. **`SYS_POST_SERVICE`** (syscall 26; testable core `sys_post_service_for_proc`) registers the caller as the `/srv/<name>` 9P server and returns a `KObj_Srv` handle — a reserve-then-commit two-phase (`srv_reserve` → `handle_alloc` → `srv_commit`, else `srv_abort` rollback) so a failed handle alloc leaves no stale entry. **Post-gate** `PROC_FLAG_MAY_POST_SERVICE` (`proc_flags` bit 4; `proc_mark_may_post_service` / `proc_may_post_service`, parallel to `PROC_FLAG_CONSOLE_ATTACHED`) — one-way, never `rfork`-propagated; an unmarked Proc cannot post or hijack `/srv/corvus`. **Tombstoning**: `exits()` → `srv_proc_exit_notify` flips the poster's `LIVE` service to `TOMBSTONED` — the name stays reserved, re-postable only by a joey-marked Proc, closing the malicious-rebind-on-restart race (the marker *is* the rebind authority). **Spec extended** — `corvus.tla` gains `service_marked` / `service_poster` (replacing the one-shot `service_posted` BOOLEAN) / `service_posters`, actions `MarkMayPost` / `PostService(p)` / `ServiceTombstone`, invariant `ServicePosterEverMarked`, and `BuggyPostWithoutMarker` + `corvus_buggy_post_without_marker.cfg`; 453 → 459 × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan runtime errors. **Self-audit clean** across the CLAUDE.md hazard categories; the formal P5-corvus-srv-impl audit is task #525, after -impl-b. **Reference**: new `docs/reference/70-devsrv.md`. **Next**: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a3 (the per-connection layer — `devsrv` walk op, kernel-minted transport pair, `SYS_SRV_ACCEPT`, `SYS_SRV_PEER`, `KObj_Srv` connection Spoor).
