- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-srv-impl-a1 landed (substantive `adb2ba8` / hash fixup `5808ad9`) — the `stripes` per-Proc identity tag + the `KObj_Srv` kobj kind, the kernel foundations of P5-corvus-srv-impl-a (the `/srv/corvus` transport; CORVUS-DESIGN §6).** `stripes` (`struct Proc`, `u64`): the kernel's unforgeable per-Proc identity tag — drawn from a monotonic `u64` counter (`g_next_stripes`) at `proc_alloc` (and `proc_init` for kproc), fresh per Proc so an `rfork` child's tag differs from its parent's (minted, never inherited); immutable for life; `stripes == 0` the reserved fail-closed sentinel (counter seeded at 1); consumed late in `proc_alloc` alongside the PID so a rolled-back alloc burns no tag (the R5-H F89 density discipline); `proc_stripes(p)` the fail-closed read API (NULL/corrupt → 0). `struct Proc` 136 → 144 B. `KObj_Srv` (`enum kobj_kind` value 9; `KOBJ_KIND_COUNT` 9 → 10): the kobj kind for a `/srv/<name>` connection Spoor — `specs/handles.tla`'s third partition `SrvKObjs`, non-transferable AND non-hardware; new `KOBJ_KIND_SRV_MASK` + three pairwise-disjoint + one completeness `_Static_assert` pinning the Tx/Hw/Srv partition; new `kobj_kind_is_srv` classifier; `handle_dup` now rejects every non-transferable kind (`!kobj_kind_is_transferable` — NoHwDup + the new NoSrvDup). **No spec change** — `corvus.tla` (`ConnRecord.peer`) + `handles.tla` (`SrvKObjs`/`SrvHandlesAtOrigin`) already model both; this implements against them. Tests: `proc.stripes_smoke` + `handles.srv_kind` (451 → 453 PASS × default + UBSan, 0 UBSan errors). Self-audit clean; the formal P5-corvus-srv-impl audit is after -impl-b. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-tsleep-scale landed (substantive `920434d` / hash fixup `f52c45e`) — the F6 fix: `timerwait_tick` one-at-a-time wake.** Closes P5-tsleep audit finding F6 (deferred): `timerwait_tick` held `g_timerwait.lock` across the per-victim `ready()`, so a herd of simultaneous `tsleep` timeouts stalled every CPU's tick behind one long lock hold. `timerwait_tick` is reworked to wake expired sleepers **one at a time** — each iteration acquires `g_timerwait.lock`, finds one expired (non-`on_cpu`) sleeper by a rescan from the list head, unlinks + wakes it under `g_timerwait.lock` + `r->lock` held continuously, then releases the global lock before the next. A herd is drained one lock-acquisition per thread; the lock is never held across N wakes. Each thread is still unlinked + woken atomically (both locks held continuously) → no `wakeup` interleaves a given wake, no ABA window — so **no spec change**: the single-waiter `tsleep.tla` `Timeout` already models one atomic per-thread wake. Keeps F7 fixed (`on_cpu` threads skipped) and resolves F9. **Audit** (opus prosecutor, focused): 0 P0/P1/P2, 3 P3 — verdict "F6 genuinely resolved"; F1 + F2 (comment precision) fixed in-chunk, F3 withdrawn. **Test**: `tsleep.herd_timeout` (3 consumers, common deadline). 450 → 451 × default + UBSan. `tsleep.tla` unchanged — re-verified clean + buggy. **Reference**: `docs/reference/16-rendez.md`. **Next**: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a.
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-tsleep landed (substantive `33bfb05` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — the deadline-bounded `Rendez` sleep.** `tsleep(r, cond, arg, deadline_ns)` is `sleep` plus an absolute deadline (`ARCH §8.8`): the wait also ends when monotonic time reaches `deadline_ns`, the return value (`TSLEEP_AWOKEN` / `TSLEEP_TIMEDOUT`) distinguishing a condition wake from a timeout. The prerequisite that keeps a hung corvus from wedging its `/srv` clients (`CORVUS-DESIGN §6.2`), and the timeout primitive the Phase-5 `poll` / `futex` work builds on. **Mechanism**: no per-deadline hardware timer — the deadline rides the existing 1 kHz scheduler tick, in the manner of Plan 9's own `tsleep`. A global timer-wait list (`g_timerwait`, `kernel/sched.c`) holds every thread inside a deadlined `tsleep`; `sched_tick()` → `timerwait_tick()` scans it each fire and times out expired sleepers. Lock order `g_timerwait.lock → Rendez.lock → CpuSched.lock`; `wakeup` reworked to take the global lock for the eager timer-wait unlink, with the wake itself (`wake_rendez_waiter`) factored out under `Rendez.lock` alone. New `struct Thread` fields (`timerwait_next` / `timerwait_prev` / `sleep_deadline` / `sleep_timedout`; 784 → 816 B); new `timer_now_ns()` + `timer_ns_to_counter()`. **Spec-first**: `specs/tsleep.tla` — a focused `scheduler.tla` sibling modelling the three-way cond ↔ wakeup ↔ timeout race; clean GREEN (`tsleep.cfg` / `tsleep_nodeadline.cfg` / `tsleep_liveness.cfg`, the last proving `TsleepTerminates` — a hung producer cannot wedge the waiter) + 4 buggy cfgs counterexampling `NoStaleTimerEntry` / `NoDoubleWake` / `TimeoutSound` / `TsleepTerminates`. **Audit** (opus prosecutor, scheduler / wait-wake surface): 0 P0, 1 P1, 4 P2, 4 P3, 2 withdrawn — no safety violation (I-9 and every `tsleep.tla` invariant held under prosecution); the P1 (`wakeup`'s global-lock hold widened across `ready()` / IPI / `on_cpu`-spin) + the matching P2 (`on_cpu` spin in IRQ context) fixed in-chunk by narrowing `g_timerwait.lock` to the unlink only; two P2s closed by documenting the deadline contract; one P2 (the `timerwait_tick` thundering-herd lock hold) deferred — a contention hazard with zero invariants broken, whose safe fix needs a generation counter + a `tsleep.tla` re-model and has no `tsleep` caller until P5-corvus-srv-impl-a. **Tests**: `kernel/test/test_tsleep.c` — 5 tests (fast-path, no-deadline degradation, past-deadline, wakeup-before-deadline, timeout-via-tick); 445 → 450 × default + UBSan. **Reference**: `docs/reference/16-rendez.md` (the `tsleep` section) + `11-timer.md`. **Next**: P5-corvus-srv-impl-a.
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-hostowner-a landed (substantive `20fa615` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — the kernel capability + console-attachment foundation for hostowner elevation.** First sub-chunk of the P5-hostowner macro-chunk (CORVUS-DESIGN §10). Defines **`CAP_HOSTOWNER`** (`caps.h`, bit 3) — an *elevation-only* capability deliberately excluded from `CAP_ALL`, so no Proc (not even kproc) holds it at creation and `rfork`'s mask-AND can never confer it; the sole grant path is corvus's ADMIN_ELEVATE verb (P5-hostowner-b). Defines **`PROC_FLAG_CONSOLE_ATTACHED`** (`proc.h`, `proc_flags` bit 3) — the kernel-stamped local-console trust anchor — plus `proc_mark_console_attached` (one-way set, ALIVE-gated; materializes `specs/corvus.tla` `MarkConsoleAttached`) and the fail-closed `proc_is_console_attached`. `joey_thunk` stamps joey (the console-login chain root) at boot, with a self-check. The console bit is **never** propagated by `rfork` — `proc_alloc` zeroes `proc_flags`, `rfork_internal` doesn't copy it — so a future remote-login chain cannot inherit the trust anchor. **No spec change** — `corvus.tla` already models `console_attached` + `MarkConsoleAttached` + `HostownerRequiresConsole`; this is the impl (`SPEC-TO-CODE.md` MarkConsoleAttached row updated to as-built). **Tests**: `proc.console_attached_smoke` — mark/query/idempotence + rfork non-propagation, including from a *console-attached* parent (the case that catches a `proc_flags`-copy regression); plus joey's boot-path self-check. 444 → 445. **Audit** (opus prosecutor, capability surface): 0 P0, 0 P1, 0 P2, 4 P3 — F1 (ALIVE-state guard on the mark) + F3 (stale `caps.h` rfork-inheritance comment) + F4 (test now exercises non-propagation from an attached parent) fixed in-chunk; F2 (non-atomic `proc_flags |=`) closed with justification — it matches the 3 existing hardening-syscall writers and is sound under the v1.0 single-thread-per-Proc invariant; the atomic conversion is a codebase-wide item for the multi-threaded-Proc lift. **Verified**: 445/445 PASS × default + UBSan (UBSan now needs `BOOT_TIMEOUT=300` — the corvus-crypto suite outgrew 180 s), 0 `EXTINCTION` lines. **Scripture gap flagged for P5-hostowner-b**: the cap-grant mechanism — how userspace corvus causes the kernel to set `CAP_HOSTOWNER` on a peer Proc — is under-specified in ARCH/CORVUS-DESIGN; it needs a design pass + signoff before -b. **Next**: P5-hostowner-b (ADMIN_ELEVATE verb + the cap-grant mechanism + admin-verb gating). Predecessor: P5-secondary-stack-guard (`78dbc36`/`8ca86b4`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-secondary-stack-guard landed (substantive `78dbc36` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — guard pages for the two stacks that lacked them.** Closes two deferred audit findings — both pre-existing gaps where a stack lacked a guard page so an overflow corrupted adjacent memory silently. **el1h audit F1**: the per-secondary boot stacks (`g_secondary_boot_stacks` — also the permanent stack of each CPU's kstack-less idle thread) had no guard page, unlike the boot CPU's `_boot_stack_guard`. Restructured from `char[7][16384]` to `struct secondary_stack[7]`, each slot `{ char guard[4096]; char usable[16384] }`, page-aligned; `build_page_tables` (mmu.c) zeroes each slot's leading guard-page L3 PTE in both `l3_kernel` and the direct-map alias; `secondary_entry` (start.S) sets SP to the slot top (stride 20480); `addr_is_stack_guard` (fault.c) recognizes the secondary guard ranges → `extinction("kernel stack overflow")`. **corvus-bringup-d audit F7**: the 256 KiB user-stack VMA had nothing reserved below it. New `vma_alloc_guard` creates a `prot==0` / `burrow==NULL` reserved guard VMA (no BURROW — outside the dual-refcount lifecycle); `exec_map_user_stack` installs a one-page guard at `[EXEC_USER_STACK_GUARD_BASE, EXEC_USER_STACK_BASE)` — an overflow faults (`userland_demand_page` rejects `prot==0` before the NULL BURROW is touched), and `vma_insert` overlap-rejection reserves the page against a future mapping allocator. Guard size 1 page for both, matching `_boot_stack_guard` (boot/idle code runs shallow stacks; `-fstack-clash-protection` blocks single-frame leaps). **No spec** — guard-page placement is page-table layout + a reserved VMA range, not a §28 concurrency invariant; `corvus.tla` and the 7 other specs unaffected. **Tests**: new `secondary_stack_guard` fault-test variant (`tools/test-fault.sh`), `smp.secondary_stack_guard_layout` (slot-layout pin), `exec.user_stack_guard` (guard VMA present + `prot==0`/`burrow==NULL` + overlap rejection); 442 → 444. **Audit** (opus prosecutor — start.S/mmu.c/fault.c/smp.c+h/vma.c/exec.c): 0 P0, 0 P1, 0 P2, 3 P3 — F2 (a sibling asm literal `#8`/`DTB_MAX_CPUS` left unpinned) fixed in-chunk with a `_Static_assert`; F1 (guard PTE index unbounded at runtime) + F3 (direct-map-KVA FAR form unrecognized) closed no-change — both consistent with the pre-existing `_boot_stack_guard` pattern. **Verified**: 444/444 PASS × default + UBSan, 0 `EXTINCTION` lines, all 5 fault-test variants PASS. Reference docs `03-mmu`/`17-smp-bringup`/`25-fault-dispatcher`/`26-vma`/`27-exec` updated; F1 closed in `67-el1h-kernel.md`, F7 in `69-corvus-unwrap.md`. **Next**: the remaining corvus verbs + `CRVS` FS persistence. Predecessor: P5-corvus-bringup-d (`cb0f849`/`a9b86c4`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-bringup-d landed (substantive `cb0f849` / hash fixup `*(pending)*`) — corvus's real ML-KEM-768 + X25519 hybrid keypair, the hybrid-PKE DEK envelope, and the WRAP + UNWRAP verbs.** Fourth corvus sub-chunk per CORVUS-DESIGN.md §6.4/§6.5. P5-corvus-bringup-c wrapped a 64-byte CSPRNG placeholder and discarded it after AUTH; -d makes the keypair a real **ML-KEM-768 (FIPS 203) + X25519 hybrid** — a 3648-byte plaintext (x25519 sk/pk + ml-kem ek/dk) generated at USER_CREATE — and has AUTH retain it in the mlock'd session slab for the two verbs that consume it. **New crates** on `aarch64-unknown-none`, all pure-Rust + explicit-RNG (no `getrandom`): `ml-kem` 0.2 (RustCrypto FIPS 203), `x25519-dalek` 2 (`static_secrets` + `zeroize`), `sha2` 0.10, `kem` 0.3.0-pre.0 (the `Encapsulate`/`Decapsulate` traits — ml-kem does not re-export them), `rand_core` 0.6; `ThylaRng` adapts `rand_core::RngCore` over `t_getrandom`. **DEK envelope** (CORVUS-DESIGN §6.5 — corvus-owned format, 1217 B): a KEM-DEM hybrid — ML-KEM-768 encapsulate ‖ X25519 ephemeral→static ECDH → a transcript-bound `SHA-256` KEK combiner → AEGIS-256 over the 32-byte DEK, AD-bound to the dataset; secure if either KEM holds. **WRAP (verb_id=10)** — new verb added to CORVUS-DESIGN §6.4 (binding scripture; user signoff) — wraps a DEK under the session user's hybrid public key. **UNWRAP (verb_id=4)**: unwraps with the secret key; the **C-7 ownership gate** (`specs/corvus.tla` `UnwrapOwnerOnly`) fires before any crypto — a cross-user UNWRAP is `PermissionDenied`. Both gate on an in-memory dataset-ownership table (USER_CREATE registers `users/<name>` → `<name>`). **Kernel**: `EXEC_USER_STACK_SIZE` 16 KiB → 256 KiB — ML-KEM-768's FO-transform decapsulate is stack-heavy and the prior 16 KiB user-stack VMA overflowed. Spec: `corvus.tla` header note (WRAP shares Unwrap's gate — no new action — comment-only); corvus.tla re-verified (clean cfg + all 5 buggy counterexample cfgs); the 7 other specs are unchanged by this chunk. Joey drives USER_CREATE michael + susan → AUTH → WRAP → UNWRAP(michael, DEK round-trip) → UNWRAP(susan) → `PermissionDenied` (C-7) → UNWRAP(ghost) → `NotFound` → SESSION_CLOSE. 442/442 PASS × default + UBSan, 0 `EXTINCTION` lines. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-el1h-kernel landed (substantive `e2784c2` / hash fixup `0e5fd1f`) — the kernel now runs uniformly at EL1h; fixes a pre-existing SMP soundness bug.** Root cause (found during P5-corvus-bringup-c boot testing): the kernel ran normal code at EL1t (`SPSel=0`) and exception handlers at EL1h (`SPSel=1`), but `cpu_switch_context` carries `SP` not `SPSel` — so under SMP work-stealing a thread could resume the `KERNEL_EXIT` exception-exit trampoline in the wrong mode, where `msr SP_EL0` against the currently-selected stack pointer is CONSTRAINED UNPREDICTABLE (`EC=0` Undefined trap; `extinction()` parks only the faulting CPU, so a secondary CPU silently died on every boot). A per-CPU exception stack was also incompatible with migrating a mid-exception thread. **Fix (Model 1)**: run the kernel uniformly at EL1h — one stack bank (`SP_EL1` = the running thread's own kernel stack), `SP_EL0` exclusively the userspace stack, exception frames built on the per-thread kernel stack so they travel with the thread (migration-safe). `cpu_switch_context` + `KERNEL_ENTRY`/`KERNEL_EXIT` are bank-agnostic and unchanged. Scripture: `ARCHITECTURE.md §12.1`/§12.2 made explicit + new invariant **I-21** (§28); `CLAUDE.md §28` mirror. Code: `start.S` (primary + secondary boot to EL1h — assert `SPSel=1` before every SP write, single kernel stack), `vectors.S` (EL1t vector group `0x000`/`0x080` → `VEC_UNEXPECTED`), `userland.S` (`userland_enter` installs the user SP via `msr sp_el0` at EL1h; the P4-Fix157 SPSel dance removed), `sched.c` (`try_steal` skips `kstack_base==NULL` bootstrap threads — audit F2), `main.c`/`smp.c`/`smp.h`/`timer.c`/`test_smp.c`/`thread.c`. Spec: new `specs/sched_ctxsw.tla` (+2 cfgs) pins I-21 — `DUAL_MODE=FALSE` (Model 1) clean, `DUAL_MODE=TRUE` (Model 2) the executable counterexample. Adversarial audit of the exception-entry + boot + scheduler surfaces: no P0; F2 (P1) + F3 (P2) fixed in-chunk; F1 (P2 — secondary-CPU boot stacks lack guard pages) deferred to a focused follow-up (pre-existing gap; bounded risk; pairs with the dedicated overflow-stack hardening item). **Verified**: 442/442 PASS × default + UBSan, **0 `EXTINCTION` lines**, 4/4 CPUs, the full joey→corvus crypto round-trip with cross-CPU work-stealing enabled. See `docs/reference/67-el1h-kernel.md`. **Next**: P5-corvus-bringup-c rebases on top. Predecessor: P5-corvus-bringup-b (`9cf92c6`/`6d9994f`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-bringup-b landed (substantive `9cf92c6` / hash fixup `6d9994f`) — `/sbin/corvus` server loop + binary frame wire codec + AUTH + SESSION_CLOSE verbs.** Second impl chunk of the corvus daemon arc per CORVUS-DESIGN.md §10. Extends -a's hardening-then-exit skeleton into a single-peer Spoor server that loops reading binary-framed verb requests on fd 0, dispatching, writing responses on fd 1; exits 0 on rx EOF. **Wire format** per CORVUS-DESIGN.md §6.4: request = `verb_id u8 + payload_len u16 LE + payload`; response = `status u8 + payload_len u16 LE + payload`. **Two verbs implemented**: AUTH (verb_id=1) parses user_len u8 + user + pass_len u16 LE + passphrase; at this skeleton the passphrase is NOT verified (Argon2id integration at P5-corvus-bringup-c) — presence + valid framing = success; mints 33-byte token (`'s'` + 32 hex chars encoding 16 bytes of CSPRNG entropy from t_getrandom); SESSION_CLOSE (verb_id=3) parses 33-byte token + clears the session if it matches. Every other verb_id returns status=BadFormat. **Session table**: single-slot at this skeleton (`static mut SESSION: Session`). The `user` and `token` fields are set once at install + never mutated until clear (structural C-3 enforcement: there is no setter that mutates `bound_user` in place; spec's BuggyAuthBindingMutate shape is unreachable). One-session-per-peer enforced via the `active` flag (spec's `AuthSuccess` precondition). Accessor wrappers use `core::ptr::addr_of!` / `addr_of_mut!` to avoid Rust 1.77+'s `static_mut_refs` lint. Payload buffer wiped via `t_explicit_bzero` between iterations as defence-in-depth for future verb additions that carry secrets. **libthyla-rs extension**: +4 Rust SVC wrappers (`t_pipe` / `t_read` / `t_write` / `t_close`) + 4 syscall consts (T_SYS_PIPE=8 .. T_SYS_CLOSE=11) + 1 forward-compat const (T_SYS_SPAWN_FULL=25). **Joey orchestration**: extended to create 2 pipes via `t_pipe`, spawn /sbin/corvus via `t_spawn_full` with `[c2s_rd, s2c_wr]` + `T_CAP_LOCK_PAGES | T_CAP_CSPRNG_READ`, drive AUTH ("michael" + skeleton passphrase) → assert OK + 33-byte token starting `'s'` → drive SESSION_CLOSE with that token → assert OK + 0-byte payload → close c2s_wr (triggers corvus EOF) → wait_pid corvus → assert status=0. **Boot log on success**: `corvus: ready (hardening applied; serving /srv/corvus/ over fd 0/1)` → `joey: AUTH ok (token=s3e02730...)` → `joey: SESSION_CLOSE ok` → `corvus: server_loop returned EOF; shutting down clean` → `joey: /sbin/corvus reaped status=0; AUTH + SESSION_CLOSE round-trip verified`. **Spec correspondence** (specs/corvus.tla at `c00de63`/`e5ce30a`): the AUTH and SESSION_CLOSE handlers materialize the `AuthSuccess(p, u)` and `SessionClose(p)` spec actions; `SessionUserImmutable` (C-3) is enforced structurally by the Rust API surface. Other actions / invariants (SessionTransfer, AdminElevate, Unwrap, AdminVerb, UnwrapOwnerOnly, AdminRequiresProcCap, HostownerRequiresConsole) require future sub-chunks. **No new audit-trigger surfaces** — corvus is userspace consuming existing audited syscalls (pipe + read + write + close + spawn-full are at the audited syscall surface). **Testing**: boot path IS the regression. AUTH + SESSION_CLOSE round-trip runs on every boot; failure at any step propagates non-zero exit. The corvus binary grew 5528B → 13304B (+ wire codec + verb handlers + session-table accessors). **Test timing**: total boot ≈ 15s under default + 25s under UBSan; if CI flakes raise to BOOT_TIMEOUT=60 (already standard for UBSan matrix). Test count 442/442 PASS × default + UBSan unchanged. **Files**: `usr/corvus/src/main.rs` (heavy extension; +280 LOC: wire constants + session table + verb handlers + server loop, replaces -a's simple post-hardening exit); `usr/lib/libthyla-rs/src/lib.rs` (+4 wrappers + 5 syscall consts; ~110 LOC); `usr/joey/joey.c` (+pipe-pair + spawn_full + AUTH/SESSION_CLOSE round-trip + close + wait; ~150 LOC); `docs/reference/66-corvus-server.md` (new ~250 LOC); `docs/REFERENCE.md` (Tip + doc-table entry 66); `docs/phase5-status.md` (row); memory updates. **Stage**: structural wire surface live; the two state-machine spec actions (AuthSuccess + SessionClose) materialized in code. **Next chunk**: P5-corvus-bringup-c (Argon2id passphrase verification + state file format `CRVS` + hybrid keypair storage; opens the door to UNWRAP at -d). - **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-bringup-a landed (substantive `7487054` / hash fixup `a4bb28c`) — `/sbin/corvus` skeleton: hardening syscalls + readiness banner + clean exit. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-audit-r15-c landed (substantive `9641281` / hash fixup `0288d98`) — closes audit F230 (P1) + F232 (P2); per-client `spin_lock_t` around every public 9P client op + `handles.tla` spec extension `RforkWithFds` + new `SpawnFdsRightsMonotonic` invariant.** F230 closure: added `spin_lock_t lock` field to `struct p9_client`. Every public `p9_client_*` op acquires the lock at entry, releases at exit — uniform across handshake/walk/clunk/lopen/lcreate/read/write/getattr/setattr/readdir/statfs/fsync/symlink/mknod/rename/readlink/link/mkdir/renameat/unlinkat + alloc_fid + is_open + inflight + close (~20 functions). `CLIENT_UNLOCK_RET(c, rc)` helper macro keeps early-return paths terse. Lock placement is client-level (not session-level) because the client owns out_buf + next_fid alongside the embedded session by value — one lock covers all mutable client state. Direct callers of `p9_session_*` below the client (typically test code) self-serialize externally. On UP at v1.0 the spin part is a no-op; SMP race detection awaits TSan enablement. No IRQ-mask variant — 9P client paths are syscall/kthread context only. F232 closure: `specs/handles.tla` extended with new action `RforkWithFds(parent, child, h, new_rights)` modeling SYS_SPAWN_WITH_FDS / SYS_SPAWN_FULL fd-inheritance + new bug class `BuggySpawnFdsElevate` skipping the rights-subset guard + new ghost VARIABLE `spawn_inherits` recording (child, kobj, parent_rights) AT inheritance time + new invariant `SpawnFdsRightsMonotonic` cross-checking child handles. Distinct from `RightsCeiling` (bounds by `origin_rights[k]`); `SpawnFdsRightsMonotonic` bounds by parent's CURRENT rights at fork time — catches the F231 shape: parent had {R}, child got {R,W} where origin had {R,W,T}. New cfg `handles_buggy_spawn_fds_elevate.cfg` produces counterexample at depth 4 in <1s. handles.cfg gained `StateConstraint` (Cardinality(handles[p]) ≤ 2 + Cardinality(spawn_inherits) ≤ 2) — the new RforkWithFds × HandleDup combinatorics expanded the state space. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-audit-r15-b landed (substantive `1025026` / hash fixup `f8f7f22`) — closes audit F233 (P1) + F234 (P2); atomic refcounts for Spoor + pipe_ring; SMP correctness for cross-Proc inheritance.** **F233 fix** (`kernel/spoor.c`): all six `c->ref` sites converted to `__atomic_*` ops. `spoor_alloc_internal` uses RELAXED init store (pre-publication safe); `spoor_ref` uses `fetch_add(ACQ_REL)` with pre <= 0 → extinction (use-after-free guard); `spoor_unref` and `spoor_clunk` use `fetch_sub(ACQ_REL)` with pre == 1 → last-drop path; `spoor_free_internal` + `spoor_clone` use ACQUIRE-load for diagnostics. **Semantic shift in spoor_clunk**: dev->close now runs AFTER the atomic decrement (ref=0, storage intact, no concurrent observers possible). Close hooks may still safely access c->aux / c->dev / c->qid — storage is valid until spoor_free_internal. **F234 fix** (`kernel/pipe.c`): same idiom applied to pipe_ring->ref. `pipe_create_internal` uses RELAXED init = 2; `devpipe_close` uses `fetch_sub(ACQ_REL)` with pre == 1 → free the ring. **Standard atomic-refcount idiom**: ACQ_REL ordering ensures all CPUs see prior writes to the resource's fields BEFORE the last-drop free; pre-value capture ensures exactly one CPU sees pre==1 even under concurrent decrement from N CPUs. **No new tests** — fixes are correctness-by-construction (atomic discipline replaces non-atomic); existing test suite (441/441 PASS × default + UBSan) is the regression — if atomic discipline broke single-threaded correctness, those tests would fail. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-spawn-caps landed (substantive `e3d34e3` / hash fixup `a5313f1`) — `SYS_SPAWN_WITH_CAPS` (= 24) for granting cap-subset to a spawned child.** ABI: `SYS_SPAWN_WITH_CAPS(name_va, name_len, cap_mask) → child_pid/-1`. Wraps the existing `rfork_with_caps` (P4-Ic3); child's caps = `parent->caps & cap_mask`. **Structural enforcement of ARCH I-2 / I-6** (caps monotonically reduce): even if cap_mask sets bits the parent doesn't hold, the AND clamps to parent's actual caps — extra bits silently dropped. Extends `SYS_SPAWN` with explicit fd inheritance: the listed fds (`KOBJ_SPOOR`-only at v1.0; ≤ SYS_SPAWN_MAX_FDS = 16; child fd 0..fd_count-1) are installed in the child's handle table BEFORE exec_setup. **Refcount discipline (load-bearing)**: handler bumps spoor_ref for each listed fd; parent retains its own holds; child gets its own independent refs via handle_alloc (which consumes the bumped ref). Failure paths drop all bumped refs symmetrically. **Why separate syscall instead of extending SYS_SPAWN**: would ABI-break the libt stub (x2/x3 garbage suddenly meaningful). Separate syscall keeps `SYS_SPAWN` shape stable; intent is explicit at the call site. **Why KOBJ_SPOOR-only at v1.0**: ARCH I-5 prohibits MMIO/IRQ/DMA cross-Proc transfer; Burrow inheritance held until v1.x. **Why explicit-list, not Plan 9 RFFDG**: cleaner for "child gets these specific fds" (joey's typical case); real SYS_RFORK with RFFDG lands when a v1.x workload (shell pipelines, musl clone() translation) needs the general primitive. **`/stub-driver`** (~110 LOC, new userspace binary): does the full production-shape orchestration entirely from EL0 — t_pipe × 2 → t_spawn_with_fds("stratumd-stub", [c2s_rd, s2c_wr], 2) → t_close driver-side copies → t_attach_9p → t_mount → t_unmount → t_close all → t_wait_pid → t_exits(0). **Kernel test** (`kernel/test/test_stub_driver.c`, ~85 LOC): minimal — just load + rfork-exec /stub-driver + wait_pid + assert status=0. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-spawn-wait landed (substantive `335d87d` / hash fixup `3915559`) — `SYS_SPAWN` (= 21) + `SYS_WAIT_PID` (= 22) syscalls; `/joey` now orchestrates `/hello` end-to-end in the production boot path.** ABI: `SYS_SPAWN(name_va, name_len) → child_pid/-1` (name ≤ SYS_SPAWN_NAME_MAX = 64; binary ≤ SYS_SPAWN_BLOB_MAX = 32 KiB; combined `rfork(RFPROC)` + `exec` against a devramfs-named binary; child inherits no caps at v1.0); `SYS_WAIT_PID(status_out_va) → reaped_pid/-1` (`status_out_va` may be NULL; per-byte `uaccess_store_u8` × 4 for the int write; mirrors `kernel/proc.c::wait_pid`). **Why combined fork+exec at v1.0**: a real `SYS_RFORK` returning 0-in-child/pid-in-parent needs COW + child-context restoration, neither of which exists yet. Plan 9's `rfork(RFPROC|RFEXEC)` idiom sidesteps both: child gets a fresh address space populated from the named binary. A separate `SYS_RFORK` lands when a v1.x workload requires it. **Lifetime discipline**: `SYS_SPAWN`'s thunk inherits ownership of two kmalloc'd buffers (blob copy + args struct); thunk frees both after `exec_setup`. On rfork failure, the parent frees them. The 8-aligned blob copy is mandatory (same R5-G F61 alignment precondition as joey + `kernel/test/test_userspace_ramfs.c`). **Factoring**: `int sys_spawn_for_proc(struct Proc *p, const char *name, size_t name_len)` extracted as a non-static inner so kernel-internal tests can drive it with kernel-resident names; SVC wrapper does user-VA validation + name copy then calls the inner. `sys_wait_pid_handler` not extracted — its only non-trivial step is the per-byte uaccess store; tests call `wait_pid()` directly. **Joey live demonstration**: `usr/joey/joey.c` extended from "exit 0" to "spawn /hello, wait_pid, verify status=0, print 'orchestration verified'". Boot log shows the four interleaved lines (`joey: rforking child for /joey... ; joey: hello from /joey... ; joey: spawned /hello pid=N ; hello from /hello... ; joey: /hello reaped status=0`). **Userspace libt stubs**: `t_spawn(name, name_len) → pid/-1`, `t_wait_pid(int *status) → pid/-1`, `T_SPAWN_NAME_MAX = 64u`. **7 new kernel-internal tests** in `kernel/test/test_sys_spawn.c`: sys_spawn.happy_path (spawn "hello" + wait_pid + status=0) + 5 rejection paths (null_name / zero_len / oversize_name / missing_binary / embedded_nul) + sys_wait_pid.no_children_returns_neg1. Each test calls `drain_zombies()` first for deterministic ordering. **No spec extension** — the orchestration shape is pure composition over `specs/scheduler.tla` (rfork + ready + wait_pid wakeup) + `specs/handles.tla` (fresh address space, no fd-table sharing). **Audit posture**: extends `kernel/syscall.c` (existing audit-trigger surface); the kmalloc-blob-copy + free pattern is symmetric and exercised by 7 tests + the live boot path. No new attack surfaces — the name uaccess uses the existing `uaccess_load_u8` + `UACCESS_USER_VA_TOP` bound; the rfork machinery is the existing audited primitive. **Files**: `kernel/include/thylacine/syscall.h` (+SYS_SPAWN=21 + SYS_WAIT_PID=22 enum entries + SYS_SPAWN_NAME_MAX + SYS_SPAWN_BLOB_MAX macros); `kernel/syscall.c` (+devramfs.h + elf.h + exec.h includes; ~110 LOC for sys_spawn_thunk + sys_spawn_for_proc + sys_spawn_handler + sys_wait_pid_handler + 2 dispatcher cases); `kernel/test/test_sys_spawn.c` (new; 7 tests; ~110 LOC); `kernel/test/test.c` (+7 forward decls + 7 registry entries); `kernel/CMakeLists.txt` (+1 test source); `usr/lib/libt/include/thyla/syscall.h` (+T_SYS_SPAWN=21 + T_SYS_WAIT_PID=22 + T_SPAWN_NAME_MAX macro + t_spawn + t_wait_pid stubs); `usr/joey/joey.c` (extended to orchestrate /hello + tiny in-place itoa_dec); `docs/reference/60-sys-spawn-wait.md` (new; ~230 LOC); `docs/REFERENCE.md` (Tip + doc-table entry 60); `docs/phase5-status.md` (row). 416 → 423 PASS × default + UBSan (BOOT_TIMEOUT=60 for UBSan). **Stage**: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup is now the natural next chunk — joey can spawn a stratumd-stub binary the same way it spawns /hello today. **Next chunks**: P5-stratumd-stub-bringup (the architectural moment — userspace stratumd-stub binary serving a tiny 9P tree; joey forks it, attaches, mounts as root, verifies) OR P5-spawn-caps (SYS_SPAWN_WITH_CAPS for granting subset of parent's caps; needed for corvus startup but can wait until P5-corvus-bringup) OR P5-stratumd-multi (Stratum-side, Michal-owned, parallel-trackable). Predecessor: P5-joey-from-ramfs (`2abe83f` / `c401ccf`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-joey-from-ramfs landed (substantive `2abe83f` / hash fixup `c401ccf`) — `/joey` is now a real userspace binary built from `usr/joey/` and shipped in the initrd cpio, replacing the 9-instruction kernel-embedded blob. Structural-not-behavioural change unblocking the P5-stratumd-bringup arc.** Files: `usr/joey/joey.c` (new; prints a banner via t_putstr, exits 0) + `usr/joey/CMakeLists.txt` (new) + `usr/CMakeLists.txt` (+add_subdirectory) + `tools/build.sh::build_ramfs` (usr_bins += "joey") + `kernel/joey.c` (build_init_elf + embedded `g_joey_program[]` removed; `joey_run` now calls `devramfs_lookup("joey", ...)` + copies into an 8-aligned static buffer `g_joey_elf_blob` before exec_setup). Reason for the static-buffer copy: cpio newc data is 4-aligned; `kernel/elf.c::elf_load` rejects 8-misaligned Ehdr per R5-G F61. Same pattern as `kernel/test/test_userspace_ramfs.c`. If /joey breaks, joey_run extincts, banner never prints, tools/test.sh reports failure. **Failure modes** documented in `docs/reference/59-joey-from-ramfs.md`: /joey missing from cpio / zero size / exceeds 32 KiB / exec_setup rc!=0 / EL0 fault. **No spec extension** — orchestration shape unchanged (rfork → exec_setup → userland_enter → wait_pid); only the source of the ELF moved. **Audit posture**: kernel/joey.c is not on the audit-trigger surface; it's an init-time orchestration helper. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-syscalls landed (substantive `0db0dcf` / hash fixup `d10d4ee`) — 5 v1.0 hardening syscalls + 2 new caps + per-Proc flags + public kernel CSPRNG API; the foundational scaffold for corvus + per-user stratumd startup per CORVUS-DESIGN.md §4.1.1.** ABI: `SYS_MLOCKALL(flags)→0/-1` (CAP_LOCK_PAGES; sets PROC_FLAG_MLOCKED) + `SYS_SET_DUMPABLE(0/1)→0/-1` (one-way to 0; sets PROC_FLAG_NODUMP) + `SYS_SET_TRACEABLE(0/1)→0/-1` (one-way to 0; sets PROC_FLAG_NOTRACE) + `SYS_EXPLICIT_BZERO(buf_va, len)→0/-1` (per-byte uaccess_store_u8; ≤4 KiB) + `SYS_GETRANDOM(buf_va, len, flags)→bytes/-1` (CAP_CSPRNG_READ; ARM RNDR-backed; ≤4 KiB). Syscall numbers 16-20; libt stubs `t_mlockall`/`t_set_dumpable`/`t_set_traceable`/`t_explicit_bzero`/`t_getrandom`. **New caps**: `CAP_LOCK_PAGES` (1<<1) + `CAP_CSPRNG_READ` (1<<2); CAP_ALL updated (kproc has all three). **Per-Proc flags**: `proc_flags` u32 + 4-byte pad added to struct Proc (128→136 bytes; static_assert updated); `PROC_FLAG_NODUMP/NOTRACE/MLOCKED` defined. **Kernel CSPRNG API**: new `kernel/include/thylacine/random.h` exposing `kern_random_bytes(buf, len) → bytes/-1` + `kern_random_seeded() → bool`. `kernel/random.c` refactored to extract `kern_random_bytes` from `devrandom_read`; `devrandom_read` is now a thin wrapper. **Forward-compat scaffolding**: at v1.0 the per-Proc flags don't gate anything because the enforcing subsystems (swap, core dumps, debug Spoors) don't exist yet. corvus calls the syscalls at startup anyway so its startup is forward-compatible; flags enforce when swap/core-dumps/debug-Spoors land in v1.x. **One-way semantics**: `SYS_SET_DUMPABLE(1)` on a Proc that already has PROC_FLAG_NODUMP is REFUSED (-1). Same for `SYS_SET_TRACEABLE`. Idempotent for the same-state direction. **6 new kernel-internal tests** in `kernel/test/test_sys_corvus.c`: sys_mlockall.cap_gate + sys_set_dumpable.one_way_to_zero + sys_set_traceable.one_way_to_zero + sys_corvus_caps.kproc_has_new_caps + kern_random.seeded_returns_true_on_qemu + kern_random.bytes_produces_nonzero (32-byte read produces ≥1 non-zero byte + two reads differ + zero-length is no-op + NULL/negative rejected). **No spec extension** — these are forward-compat hardening syscalls; their semantic invariants (mlock pages don't page out; NODUMP Procs don't core dump; NOTRACE Procs reject debug attach) become spec-pinned when their enforcing subsystems land in v1.x. **Audit posture**: extends kernel/syscall.c (existing trigger surface) + adds kernel/random.c (CSPRNG public API). No new attack surfaces — kern_random_bytes is internal-API-only-now; SYS_GETRANDOM's user-VA bounce uses the existing uaccess_store_u8 with the existing UACCESS_USER_VA_TOP bound + fault-fixup. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-corvus-design landed (substantive `fc9cf47` / hash fixup `cf45eca`) — binding scripture for the post-pivot stack: `docs/CORVUS-DESIGN.md` (~930 LOC) + cross-references from ARCH §5 + §11.2b + §14.3a + §15.2/§15.3/§15.4 + §28 + §29 + ROADMAP §7.2a.** Captures the six v1.0 design decisions (D1: classic ESP, D2: integrity-only system pool with HKDF boot-key device binding, D3: always-encrypted user datasets, D4: Order-C boot with per-user stratumd, D5: no-UID-0 hostowner + recovery phrase, D6: explicit v1.0 acceptance of no-boot-chain-integrity; Secure Boot v1.1). **Architectural reframing from earlier draft**: corvus is a Thylacine-native daemon, NOT a port of Stratum's janus — draws design influence from factotum, janus, FileVault, ZFS, fscrypt. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-attach-probe landed (substantive `029016b` / hash fixup `106edeb`) — userspace integration test of the Phase 5 mount surface; `/attach-probe` ELF binary + kernel-thread 9P responder + test framework. End-to-end SYS_ATTACH_9P + SYS_MOUNT + SYS_UNMOUNT driven through a real EL0 Proc against a real wire-codec / dev9p / spoor-transport / pipe stack — until this chunk, every Phase 5 test ran via kernel-internal loopback shortcuts.** Probe (`usr/attach-probe/attach-probe.c`, ~14.9 KiB ELF) expects fd 0 (tx) + fd 1 (rx) pre-installed in its handle table by the kernel test framework, calls t_attach_9p("/", 1, 0) → t_mount(99, 0) → t_unmount(99) → t_unmount(99 — expect fail) → t_close(attach_fd) → t_close(0) → t_close(1) → t_putstr("attach-probe: PASS\n") → t_exits(0). **Kernel responder** (in `kernel/test/test_attach_probe.c`, ~280 LOC) is a kproc kthread that owns the OTHER ends of the two pipe pairs; loop reads framed Tmsgs from rx → builds responses via inline switch (Tversion → Rversion msize=4096 + "9P2000.L"; Tattach → Rattach qid; Tclunk → Rclunk; anything else → Rlerror EIO) → writes to tx. Exits cleanly on rx EOF (probe closed tx_fd → write_eof on c2s ring → wakeup). **Why kernel-thread, not two userspace Procs**: v1.0 rfork supports RFPROC only; RFFDG (shared fd table — needed to give two Procs access to the same pipe pair) is deferred. Cross-Proc Spoor transfer is gated on RIGHT_TRANSFER through a 9P session per ARCH I-4 — circular dependency. When RFFDG lands later, the test can graduate to a two-proc design. **Refcount discipline (load-bearing)**: each pipe_create Spoor's ref=1 is TRANSFERRED (not bumped) to its owner — responder gets c2s_rd + s2c_wr; probe's handle table gets c2s_wr (fd 0) + s2c_rd (fd 1) via handle_alloc's ref-consumption convention. Boot retains zero refs after setup. If boot held a residual ref on c2s_wr, the probe's t_close(tx_fd) would drop to 1 (not 0), devpipe_close wouldn't fire, write_eof wouldn't be set, responder would block forever in dev_read — surfaced by an earlier draft of the test; documented as caveat #1 in `57-attach-probe.md`. **Mid-chunk discovery**: Tclunk on root_fid is rejected at the session layer (`kernel/9p_session.c::p9_session_send_clunk` line 303 — root fids are session-scoped, cleaned up implicitly at session close, not via wire Tclunk). p9_attached_destroy already tolerates this via `(void)p9_client_clunk(...)`. The probe's t_close(attach_fd) → dev9p_close → p9_attached_destroy → attempted Tclunk silently rejected; the responder sees exactly 2 messages (Tversion + Tattach), not 3. Test asserts `>= 2` and documents the design intent at the assertion site. **Build wiring**: `usr/attach-probe/` (new module: 1 C source + 1 CMakeLists) + `usr/CMakeLists.txt` (add_subdirectory) + `tools/build.sh` (usr_bins array += "attach-probe") + `kernel/CMakeLists.txt` (test_attach_probe.c in KERNEL_SRCS) + `kernel/test/test.c` (extern + registry entry `userspace.attach_probe_round_trip`). **No spec extension** — pure composition over already-spec'd 9P client + pipe + handle layers; Tclunk-on-root rejection is a documented session-layer policy not a new invariant. **Audit posture**: extends existing audit-trigger surfaces (kernel/test/* not on the trigger list; the only kernel-source change is the test file itself). The probe binary at EL0 has no new attack surface — it uses existing syscalls with valid argument shapes. **Test count** 409 → 410; **410/410 PASS × default + UBSan** (with `BOOT_TIMEOUT=60` for UBSan — adds ~3× per-test overhead). **Stage**: Phase 5's userspace-visible mount/attach surface is now empirically validated end-to-end at EL0. **Next chunks**: P5-stratumd (boot ordering + .key sidecar design pass — now-feasible end-to-end; needs architectural design discussion) OR P5-fd-syscalls-RFFDG (graduate the attach-probe to a two-userspace-Proc design) OR codec extensions P5-wire-lock/-xattr/-stratum-ext (mechanical; low-priority). Predecessor: P5-mount-syscall (`bb778e6` / `fb4c2cd`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-mount-syscall landed (substantive `bb778e6` / hash fixup `fb4c2cd`) — `SYS_MOUNT = 14` + `SYS_UNMOUNT = 15` SVC handlers + companion `spoor_clunk` Plan-9-cclose fix; the last deferred SVC handler from Phase 5's plan. With this chunk every user-visible mount/attach syscall from ARCH §11.2 is live.** ABI: `SYS_MOUNT(source_spoor_fd, target_path_id, flags) → 0/-1`; `SYS_UNMOUNT(target_path_id) → 0/-1`. Thin wrappers over `kernel/territory.c::mount` / `::unmount`. **target_path_id** is a u32 abstract path token at v1.0 (the same `path_id_t` used by the existing bind/unbind/mount/unmount C-API + `struct PgrpMount`); string-path resolution lands with the future walk subsystem. **flags** mirror Plan 9 (`MREPL` / `MBEFORE` / `MAFTER` / `MCREATE`); only `MREPL` has distinguished semantics at v1.0. **Rights gate**: source handle requires `RIGHT_READ` (a mount holder consumes the source's tree). **Companion fix**: `kernel/spoor.c::spoor_clunk` switched from "run dev->close on every clunk" to Plan 9 cclose semantics — `dev->close` runs ONLY when the ref hits 0. Prior behavior would have torn down per-Spoor Dev state (pipe endpoints, 9P sessions) on the user's first close even while a mount-table entry held a reference; P5-mount-syscall is the first feature where that asymmetry becomes wrong. Site-changes: `kernel/territory.c` switched 3 spoor_unref → spoor_clunk (unmount, mount-MREPL displacement, territory_unref final-release); `kernel/dev9p.c::dev9p_close` switched 2 spoor_unref → spoor_clunk (transport-Spoor cleanup). Constructor-failure + attach_9p rollback sites kept on spoor_unref (no last-drop semantics needed). **Userspace stubs** `t_mount` + `t_unmount` in libt's syscall.h match the kernel ABI shape; `T_MREPL`/`T_MBEFORE`/`T_MAFTER`/`T_MCREATE` flag macros mirror the kernel side. **Tests** in `kernel/test/test_sys_mount.c` (9 tests): happy_path_grafts_pipe_spoor + idempotent_on_duplicate + rejects_bad_fd + rejects_missing_right_read + rejects_invalid_flags + rejects_null_territory + unmount.removes_entry_and_drops_ref + unmount.rejects_nonexistent_target + caller_close_keeps_mount_alive (the **end-to-end lifecycle test** that validates the Plan 9 cclose fix — mount, close source fd, close other pipe end, ring stays alive; Territory drop frees the ring). **No spec extension** — `specs/territory.tla::MountRefcountConsistency` is preserved structurally by the territory.c primitives; spoor_clunk semantics are an implementation refinement orthogonal to the spec's abstract refcount drop. **Audit posture**: extends `kernel/syscall.c` (existing) + `kernel/territory.c` (existing — joined trigger list at P5-attach-mount) + `kernel/dev9p.c` (existing — joined at P5-attach-dev) + `kernel/spoor.c` (existing — Spoor lifecycle). No new attack surfaces — handlers thin-wrap already-audited primitives. **Test count** 400 → 409; **409/409 PASS × default + UBSan**. **Stage**: Phase 5's user-visible mount/attach surface is complete. **Next chunks**: P5-attach-probe (userspace integration test with a 9P-responder companion) + P5-stratumd (boot ordering + .key sidecar design pass — now-feasible; all kernel primitives in place) OR codec extensions P5-wire-lock/-xattr/-stratum-ext (mechanical; deferred low-priority). - **Earlier tip**: **P5-attach-syscall landed (substantive `ae0746e` / hash fixup `88cf9c3`) — `SYS_ATTACH_9P = 13` SVC handler; the user-visible body of ARCH §9.6.1's `attach_9p`. Closed the last deferred SVC handler from the P5-attach plan.** ABI: tx_fd (x0), rx_fd (x1), aname_va (x2), aname_len (x3 ≤ 256), n_uname (x4); returns KOBJ_SPOOR fd for the 9P tree's root in x0, -1 on failure. dev9p_priv gains `attached_owner` + `adapter_to_free` — on root Spoors created by SYS_ATTACH_9P, dev9p_close tears down the entire attach session. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-fd-syscalls landed (substantive `5fd72f6` / hash fixup `3948bd4`) — `SYS_CLOSE` + `SYS_DUP` SVC handlers + `/pipe-probe` userspace binary; the byte I/O composition is now empirically live in the boot log.** Kernel: `SYS_CLOSE`(=11) thin wrapper over handle_close (KOBJ_SPOOR release path from P5-fd-pipe runs spoor_clunk); `SYS_DUP`(=12) wraps handle_dup with rights validation (RightsCeiling check rejects elevation; KOBJ_SPOOR acquire path bumps spoor_ref). **Userspace**: libt's `<thyla/syscall.h>` extended with t_pipe/t_read/t_write/t_close/t_dup inline-asm stubs (matches the existing always_inline pattern). **First userspace test binary** `/pipe-probe`: 16 KiB ELF that exercises pipe→write→read→verify FIFO→dup with reduced rights→reject rights-elevation→close dup→close rd→close wr→read on closed fd→double-close, then puts `"pipe-probe: PASS\n"` + exits 0. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-fd-rw landed (substantive `54d900b` / hash fixup `a134782`) — `SYS_READ` + `SYS_WRITE` SVC handlers + `uaccess_store_u8` primitive; userspace can finally exchange bytes through fds.** ABI: `SYS_READ`(=9) and `SYS_WRITE`(=10) each take fd in x0, buf_va in x1, len in x2; return bytes transferred (>=0; 0 EOF for read) in x0, -1 on error. Per-call cap = `SYS_RW_MAX = 4096` bytes (matches PIPE_BUF_SIZE; userspace loops for larger transfers). **Rights gates**: SYS_READ requires RIGHT_READ on the handle; SYS_WRITE requires RIGHT_WRITE. SYS_PIPE grants both on both ends → pipe fds pass both gates. **User-VA validation**: same bound as SYS_PUTS (`UACCESS_USER_VA_TOP = 1<<47`); NULL / overflow rejected. Handlers factored into `sys_{read,write}_for_proc(p, h, kbuf, len)` inners — tested with kernel-side buffers bypassing the SVC + uaccess path. **uaccess_store_u8 primitive**: symmetric to `uaccess_load_u8`. Single-byte STRB with fixup table entry; same fault-recovery dispatcher path (which already handles WRITE faults via `userland_demand_page`'s VMA prot check). C decl in `arch/arm64/uaccess.h`. **Audit-trigger surface extended**: kernel/syscall.c (existing) gains read/write handlers; arch/arm64/uaccess.S (existing) gains store_u8 + fixup-table entry. **4 new kernel-internal tests**: write_then_read_round_trip (7-byte payload writes via SYS_WRITE; reads back via SYS_READ; FIFO order preserved — **canonical end-to-end test of the byte I/O path**) + rights_check (bad fd → -1) + zero_length_validates_fd (0-len call on bad fd → -1; on good fd → 0; POSIX discipline) + read_after_close_returns_eof (close wr, read empty pipe → 0 — **composes SYS_READ with specs/pipe.tla ReadEof action**). **No spec extension** — pure composition over specs/handles.tla + specs/pipe.tla. Test count 393 → 397; **397/397 PASS × default + UBSan**. **Next chunks**: P5-fd-close (SYS_CLOSE wrapper over handle_close — thin) + P5-fd-dup (SYS_DUP wrapping handle_dup; uses KOBJ_SPOOR acquire path) + P5-fd-pipe-probe (userspace probe binary exercising SYS_PIPE + SYS_READ + SYS_WRITE + SYS_CLOSE end-to-end with a libt-linked C test). Predecessor: P5-fd-pipe (`0f66f5c` / `65293f5`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P5-fd-pipe landed (substantive `0f66f5c` / hash fixup `65293f5`) — `SYS_PIPE` SVC handler + KOBJ_SPOOR release/acquire wiring; first userspace consumer of the kernel pipe primitive.** SYS_PIPE = 8: no args; allocates a `pipe_create` pair, installs both Spoors as KOBJ_SPOOR handles in the caller's HandleTable with RIGHT_READ\|WRITE\|TRANSFER. Returns rd fd in x0, wr fd in x1; -1 in x0 on failure (full rollback of partial state). **Wires KOBJ_SPOOR into handle.c**: `handle_release_obj` now `spoor_clunk`s KOBJ_SPOOR (so handle_close + proc_free's handle_table_free both tear down the underlying Spoor); `handle_acquire_obj` `spoor_ref`s (so handle_dup gives the second handle its own ref). The first kobj kind beyond BURROW + hw kinds to be reference-counted on the handle table. **Handler factored into `sys_pipe_for_proc(p, *rd, *wr)`** as the non-static inner; SVC wrapper picks up current Proc + writes ctx->regs[0/1]. **No user-VA fd[2] pointer** — uses x0 + x1 return regs to sidestep adding uaccess_store_u32 (only uaccess_load_u8 exists today); the libc shim (Phase 6+) adapts to POSIX pipe(2)'s buffer-style API. **3 kernel-internal tests**: allocates_two_distinct_spoor_handles (returns 0; distinct fds; KOBJ_SPOOR; rights match; obj pointers distinct), proc_free_releases_handles (Proc cleanup releases the ring + both Spoors — end-to-end test of the new KOBJ_SPOOR release path; pipe_total_freed += 1, spoor_total_freed += 2), handle_close_releases_one_end (closing one fd drops ring's per-end ref; closing both frees the ring). **No spec extension** — pure composition over `specs/handles.tla` (HandleAlloc + HandleClose actions) + `specs/pipe.tla` (already covered). **Audit posture**: extends the kernel/syscall.c surface + the kernel/handle.c surface (both already on the trigger list); no new attack surfaces — the wiring is mechanical. **Pre-existing extinction** at boot (joey-side trap; observed identical on baseline pre-commit; verified via git stash) is NOT a regression. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-pipe-blocking landed (substantive `431db3a` / hash fixup `92be8b6`) — `specs/pipe.tla` + extended `kernel/pipe.c`: blocking read/write with rendez integration; the missed-wakeup-freedom property (ARCH §28 I-9) is now spec-pinned for the pipe's wait/wake protocol.** Per CLAUDE.md spec-first policy: this is the chunk that opens the wait/wake invariant scope. New `specs/pipe.tla` (~225 LOC) with 4 buggy variants modeling the bug class "elide the wake-after-mutation step": BuggyWriteAppendNoWake / BuggyReadDrainNoWake / BuggyCloseWriteNoWake / BuggyCloseReadNoWake. 5 invariants — TypeOk + SingleWaiter + EofMonotonic + NoStuckReader + NoStuckWriter — the last two specialize I-9 to the pipe's two-direction state machine. TLC verdicts: 1 clean + 4 buggy-violations. **C-side**: `struct pipe_ring` gains `spin_lock_t lock`, `read_eof`/`write_eof` bool flags, two `struct Rendez` wait queues. Header 32→72 B; total 4128→4168 B. devpipe_read becomes a `for(;;) { lock + check + drain-or-eof-or-sleep + unlock + wakeup }` loop using `sleep(rendez, cond_can_read, ring)`; devpipe_write symmetric with cond_can_write. devpipe_close sets the appropriate EOF flag under lock, drops lock, calls wakeup on the OTHER side's rendez (so any sleeper exits with EOF / EPIPE), then handles refcount + free. **Compositional proof**: `specs/scheduler.tla::NoMissedWakeup` proves the atomic cond-check + sleep transition at the rendez API surface; `specs/pipe.tla::NoStuckReader/Writer` proves the pipe-side discipline of "every mutation that could enable a waiter MUST issue a wakeup." Together they close the missed-wakeup hazard end-to-end. **4 new multi-thread tests** in `kernel/test/test_pipe_blocking.c` mirroring the test_rendez_basic_handoff pattern (consumer thread does blocking op + sleeps; boot does wake-triggering action + sched()s to consumer): write_wakes_sleeping_reader + read_wakes_sleeping_writer + close_write_end_wakes_reader_with_eof + close_read_end_wakes_writer_with_epipe. Existing 2 tests with non-blocking semantics (read_on_empty_returns_zero / write_to_full_returns_zero) repurposed to test EOF / EPIPE paths (close other end FIRST to avoid blocking). **Mid-chunk bugs**: pipe_ring _Static_assert miscounted header (80 vs actual 72); fix: walked alignment math 4+4+8+8+8+1+1+(pad 2)+4+(pad 4)+16+16=72. **kernel/pipe.c joins the audit-trigger surface** alongside the wait/wake hazard category. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-pipe landed (substantive `23acfbf` / hash fixup `7f95cd0`) — `kernel/pipe.{c,h}`: Plan 9 `pipe(fd[2])` primitive at the kernel layer; connected pair of Spoors backed by a shared in-kernel ring buffer.** Replaces the test-only `test_pipe_dev` scaffold from P5-spoor-transport with the production primitive. `struct pipe_ring { magic, ref, count, head, tail, buf[PIPE_BUF_SIZE=4096] }` (4128 B; kmalloc routes through alloc_pages); `struct pipe_endpoint { magic, ring *, is_read_end }` (16 B; SLUB cached). Two Spoors share one ring; each Spoor's `aux` points at its own endpoint; the Dev vtable's read/write dispatches on `is_read_end`. **Semantics at v1.0 (non-blocking)**: read returns bytes available (0..n), 0 on empty; write returns bytes accepted (0..n), 0 on full; wrong-end (read on write-end / write on read-end) returns -1. **Blocking variant deferred to P5-pipe-blocking** — needs rendez integration + spec extension (the missed-wakeup hazard, ARCH §28 I-9, enters scope when wait/wake is wired). **Lifecycle**: ring ref=2 at create; each Spoor's close drops the ring ref; ring freed at 0. devpipe_close also frees the endpoint priv. **dc='|'** matches Plan 9 9front devpipe + the shell pipe glyph. **10 new unit tests** including the canonical e2e composition test (`pipe.compose_with_spoor_transport`) — two pipe pairs wired into a `p9_spoor_transport` adapter run Tversion + Tattach through real pipes, proving the entire 9P stack composes against the production byte-pipe primitive. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-attach-mount landed (substantive `c21d002` / hash fixup `178866f`) — Territory mount table + `mount` / `unmount` kernel primitives + `specs/territory.tla` extension for mount-lifecycle invariants.** Per ARCH §9.6.6: every filesystem entity is a Spoor; `mount(territory, source_spoor, target_path, flags)` grafts a Spoor at a path in a Territory, holding one refcount per entry; `unmount(territory, target_path)` removes one entry and drops the ref. Spec extension adds the `Mount` / `Unmount` / `BuggyMountNoRefbump` / `BuggyUnmountNoRefdrop` / `BuggyDestroyLeak` actions over a `mounts: [Procs -> SUBSET (Paths X Spoors)]` state layer + a `refcount: [Spoors -> Nat]` variable; `MountRefcountConsistency` is the global invariant (the kernel's per-Spoor counter must equal the cardinality of mount entries referencing it). **1 clean cfg + 4 buggy cfgs** — clean 2.56M states; each buggy cfg produces a counterexample at depth 2-3 / under 1000 states. **C-side**: `struct PgrpMount { source *, target, flags }` (16 B); `struct Territory` extended with `nmounts` + `mounts[PGRP_MAX_MOUNTS=8]` (216 B total, was 80). **Rename**: `unmount(territory, src, dst)` → `unbind(territory, src, dst)` (the inverse of bind); the verb `unmount` is now reserved for the mount-table primitive. **Lifecycle integration**: `territory_clone` deep-copies mounts AND `spoor_ref`'s each entry; `territory_unref` final-release loops mounts and `spoor_unref`'s each before `kmem_cache_free`. **`mount`** is idempotent under `(target, source)` equality; **MREPL** semantics drop-old-take-new when an entry at the target already exists; MBEFORE/MAFTER/MCREATE are stored for future union walk. **7 new unit tests** cover smoke + idempotency + MREPL replace + unmount-missing + table-full + clone-bumps-refs + destroy-drops-all-refs. **No new attack surfaces** at the SVC layer (the kernel-internal API is exercised only via tests at v1.0; the user-visible `mount` syscall is deferred to P5-fd-syscalls). **`kernel/territory.c` joins the audit-trigger surface table** in CLAUDE.md / ARCH §25.4. - **Earlier tip**: **P5-transport landed (substantive `3f7c0e2` / hash fixup `6a81bb7`) — `kernel/9p_transport.c` + `kernel/9p_transport_loopback.c`: frame-aware byte pipe + in-memory loopback backend + session composition helper.** New vtable-driven transport (`struct p9_transport_ops { send, recv, close, ctx }`) sitting between session and any backend. **Responsibilities**: frame discipline (outbound `header.size == len` validation; inbound 7-byte-header peek then body-length aggregation), partial-read aggregation (the recv core loops on `ops->recv` until a complete frame is in hand — relevant for any stream-socket backend), state machine (INIT → OPEN → CLOSED + ERROR sink), session composition (`p9_transport_exchange` = `session.send_*` + `transport.send` + `transport.recv` + `session.dispatch_rmsg` in one call). **Loopback backend** (test scaffold): in-memory pipe where each `ops->send` call invokes a caller-supplied responder fn that synthesizes the response into a caller-provided staging buffer; `chunk_size` knob forces partial-read tests through the transport's recv loop. - **Earlier tip**: **P4-Z landed (`821b047` / `86270a6`) — cumulative driver-model audit close.** R14 prosecutor pass across the 4 composed userspace drivers (`virtio-blk-rw`, `virtio-net-loop`, `virtio-input`, `virtio-gpu`) + the `libthyla-rs` runtime crate surfaced **0 P0 + 1 P1 + 3 P2 + 6 P3**; 10 closed in-commit, 2 deferred with rationale. **Closes ROADMAP §6.2 final exit criterion** ("No P0/P1 audit findings on driver model"). **F217 (P1)**: VIRTIO 1.2 §2.7.13.2 requires a driver-side LoadLoad barrier between reading `used.idx` and the subsequent `used.ring[k]` / data-buffer reads. Without it, an out-of-order ARM Cortex-A core may speculate the data reads before the used.idx load, returning pre-advance bytes. The smoking-gun exploit is virtio-input's busy-poll drain — a genuine EV_KEY/30/1 wake would be classified as phantom EV_SYN (zero type/code/value from the populate_eventq pre-zeroed slot), silently dropping the key. IRQ-driven paths (blk-rw / net-loop / gpu) are NOT safe by accident — `eret` is a Context Synchronization Event, not a memory barrier. Fix applied uniformly: new `libthyla_rs::virtio_rmb()` helper (`dmb ishld`) inserted after every `read16(used_va + 2)`; matches Linux's `virtio_rmb()` codegen. Post-build `llvm-objdump | grep -c "dmb.*ishld"` regression confirms 1/2/1/1 across blk-rw/net-loop/input/gpu. **F218 (P2)**: `INT_USED_BUFFER` vs `INT_CONFIG_CHANGE` bit-discriminated wake loop (per VIRTIO 1.2 §4.2.5; cap `MAX_NON_USED_BUFFER_WAKES = 16`); applied in blk-rw + net-loop + gpu. **F219 (P2)**: `MAX_DRAIN_PER_BATCH = QUEUE_SIZE` cap on drain loops in virtio-net-loop. **F220 (P2)**: `avail_idx_at_entry` capture replaces read-from-self gate in virtio-input. **6 × P3 also closed** (F222 doc drift; F223 discarded errno; F224 unused-var hygiene; F226 used.elem.len validation; F227 compile-asserts in blk-rw + net-loop; F228 new `T_RIGHT_HW_ALLOWED`). **2 deferred** (F221 withdrawn during pass — subsumed by F217+F219; F225 QueueReady-before-populate spec-canonical-but-safe via DRIVER_OK gate, deferred to Phase 4 housekeeping or Phase 5+). No new kernel surface; no new syscalls. **Audit-bearing at the composition layer** (CLAUDE.md "Composed-driver discipline" extension documented at 39-hw-handles.md caveat #11). Binary sizes uniformly +120-400 B (within 16-KiB blob cap): blk-rw 12976 B, net-loop 13224 B, input 12936 B, gpu 15152 B. 243/243 PASS × default + UBSan; test count unchanged (F217's regression is post-build binary inspection — the spec-violation memory-ordering bug cannot be reproduced deterministically on QEMU TCG, so binary inspection is the durable regression). Closed list at `memory/audit_r14_p4z_closed_list.md`. Predecessor: P4-K-events (`a859abc` / `7cc6c14`).

- **Earlier tip**: **P4-image-shrink landed (`eb7ed3a` / `92e8625`) — C-side `-z max-page-size=4096` + shrink all 9 legacy 96-KiB blob caps to 16 KiB.** Mirror of the Rust-side flag landed at P4-K: adds `-Wl,-z,max-page-size=4096` to `cmake/Toolchain-aarch64-userspace.cmake::THYLACINE_USERSPACE_LD_FLAGS`. ld.lld defaults to MAXPAGESIZE 0x10000 (64 KiB) on aarch64; without this flag the C-side `hello` binary carried a 64-KiB zero-padded gap between text and data PT_LOAD segments (file size 73912 B; FileSiz 0x88 at Offset 0x10000). - **Earlier tip**: **P4-L landed (`e66c033` / `1a9c882`) — virtio-gpu probe: fourth composed userspace driver; substrate generalizes to the VIRTIO GPU class.** New userspace binary `usr/virtio-gpu/` (~430 LOC Rust) drives QEMU virt's `virtio-gpu-device` end-to-end through DRIVER_OK + GET_DISPLAY_INFO using the full composed hw-handle SVC surface (MMIO + DMA + IRQ — virtio-gpu becomes the second composed driver after virtio-blk to exercise all three). What's new vs. predecessors: (1) **Two virtqueues** — controlq (idx 0) for command/response traffic + cursorq (idx 1) for cursor updates. First composed driver to configure more than one queue; `configure_queue()` helper writes the per-queue PA tuple + QueueReady transition for each, both before DRIVER_OK. (2) **controlq command/response chain** — 2-descriptor split: descriptor 0 = device-readable request hdr (24 B `virtio_gpu_ctrl_hdr` per §5.7.6.6), descriptor 1 = device-writable response payload (408 B `virtio_gpu_resp_display_info` per §5.7.6.1). NEXT linkage between them; the resp.hdr.type field returns OK_DISPLAY_INFO (0x1101) or an ERR variant in the same 24-byte hdr — virtio-gpu folds status into the response header rather than using a separate status byte like virtio-blk's 3-descriptor chain. (3) **Flat le32 config-space** at offset 0x100..0x110 (events_read / events_clear / num_scanouts / num_capsets); distinct from virtio-input's selector indirection and virtio-net's MAC+status struct. The probe issues `VIRTIO_GPU_CMD_GET_DISPLAY_INFO` via controlq, waits IRQ, verifies `resp.hdr.type == OK_DISPLAY_INFO`, then logs `num_scanouts` + `pmodes[0]` dimensions + `enabled` flag (informational; QEMU `-nographic` reports `num_scanouts=1`, `pmodes[0]=1280x800`, `enabled=1`). `tools/run-vm.sh` wires `-device virtio-gpu-device,id=gpu0` between `input_flags` and `virtio-rng-device,id=rng0`; virtio-gpu lands at slot 28 (INTID 76), rng drops to slot 27. - **Earlier tip**: **P4-Ic-latency landed (substantive `308ac55` / hash fixup `93a3b8c`) — IRQ-to-userspace latency benchmark; closes ROADMAP §6.2 exit criterion (infrastructure side).** New userspace binary `usr/irq-bench/` (~120 LOC Rust) subscribes to SPI 96, reads kernel-supplied num_iter, loops on `t_irq_wait` + `mrs cntpct_el0` + writes to shared region. Two thresholds: bare-metal target `p99 < 5 µs` per VISION §4.5 (logged for reference), CI sanity budget `p99 < 50 ms` (the actual `TEST_ASSERT`; catches pathological regressions without coupling pass/fail to QEMU TCG emulation overhead). N=128 iterations (first discarded as warmup; 127 valid samples → p99 = floor(127×0.99) = 125th sorted). Cache coherence between kernel direct-map alias and child-mapping alias is automatic (AArch64 PIPT data caches → same PA = same cache line). Cross-CPU ordering: kernel test reads `user_ts[]` only after `wait_pid`, by which time the child's exit path has driven multiple `DSB SY` barriers through `scheduler.c`. On QEMU TCG, observed p99 ≈ 7-10 ms (emulation overhead dominates; benchmark INFRASTRUCTURE is the deliverable, bare-metal authoritative measurement deferred to Phase 5+ hardware bring-up). Boot impact ~1.0 s at N=128. New reference doc `docs/reference/41-irq-bench.md`. **Audit-bearing per CLAUDE.md trigger surfaces** (Exception entry + Scheduler + Capability checks at the test-composition layer); self-audit clean across lock-ordering / lifetime / error-path / state-machine / idempotency / boundary / measurement-methodology / statistical-correctness categories. 239 → 240 tests; PASS × default (~1420 ms; +980 ms vs baseline) + UBSan (~1410 ms); 5/5 default stress. - **Earlier tip**: **R12-uaccess landed (`32367d1` substantive; `b5de03f` hash fixup) — kernel-side uaccess-fault recovery + `pretouch_rodata_pages()` workaround retired across all userspace crates.** New `arch/arm64/uaccess.{S,c,h}` exports `uaccess_load_u8(user_va, *out)` — kernel-mode user-VA accessor primitive that returns 0 on success / -1 on translation/permission fault. The asm primitive's `ldrb` is registered in a `.uaccess_fixup` table (Linux `__ex_table`-style PC-relative s32 offsets so the entries are PIE-clean — no R_AARCH64_ABS64 runtime relocs). `exception_sync_curr_el` now recognizes kernel-mode sync faults whose FAR is in the user-VA half AND whose faulting PC is in the fixup table; on hit it first calls `userland_demand_page` synthetically against the current Proc (typical case: the page is in a VMA but not yet PTE-installed → install + ERET re-executes the load), and on demand-page failure sets `ctx->elr := fixup_pc` so the primitive returns -1. `sys_puts_handler` rewritten to read bytes via `uaccess_load_u8` instead of direct kernel-mode dereference. Vector slots 0x000 + 0x200 (Sync at current EL) switched from `b _torpor` to `b .Lexception_return` so the Sync path can now return normally (previously every sync was assumed to extinct). 4 new tests in `kernel/test/test_uaccess.c`: `fixup_table_well_formed`, `fixup_lookup_known`, `fixup_lookup_unknown_returns_zero`, `load_u8_unmapped_user_va_returns_minus1` (drives a real translation fault from kproc context to validate end-to-end recovery). - **Earlier tip**: **R12-vaddr landed (`688119f` substantive; `7f78820` hash fixup) — unified `burrow_map` upper-bound check; closes F180 (R12-DMA deferred) + lifts R10 F158 MMU-layer-only-reject decision.** Adds `USER_VA_TOP = (1ull << 47)` to `arch/arm64/mmu.h` (ARM IHI 0487 D5.2.4 — 48-bit VAs without TBI; TTBR0 user-half is bits [46:0]; bit 47 is the TTBR selector). Adds `if (vaddr + length > USER_VA_TOP) return -1;` to `burrow_map` immediately after the existing overflow guard, pinned by `_Static_assert(USER_VA_TOP == (1ull << 47), ...)` so future drift in either bound surfaces at compile time. - **Earlier tip**: **R12-FP formal audit close landed — Thread SLUB align + new FP regression test + ISB after FPCR + CPACR defensive mask (2 P2 + 2 P3 all closed).** Closes R12-FP deferred audit (carried since P4-Ic5-FP). Adversarial prosecutor surfaced 0 P0 + 0 P1 + **2 P2** + 2 P3. **F165 (P2)**: Thread SLUB cache alignment hardcoded as 8; `cpu_switch_context`'s STP/LDP-Q pairs require 16-byte alignment per ARM ARM C7.2.348. Today's 784-byte Thread is a multiple of 16 by coincidence; future field addition could silently misalign object N>0 and corrupt the first context switch. Fix: pass `_Alignof(struct Thread)` so SLUB honors the struct's declared alignment. **F166 (P2)**: zero test coverage of FP save/restore. Empirically: `llvm-objdump -d` of all userspace ELFs shows ZERO FP/SIMD instructions — the claimed indirect coverage was false. Fix: new `kernel/test/test_fp.c` (~250 LOC) with two tests — `fp.cpacr_enabled` verifies FPEN=0b11 + ZEN/SMEN/TTA=0 (also pins F168); `fp.round_trip_v_regs_fpsr_fpcr` loads V0..V31 + FPCR + FPSR with a sentinel, switches into a helper that deliberately clobbers, switches back, asserts byte-by-byte equality. The clobber is what makes the test sensitive. Uses `__attribute__((target("+fp+simd")))` per function (kernel-wide `-mgeneral-regs-only` blocks codegen-level FP). **F167 (P3)**: cpu_switch_context lacked `isb` after MSR FPCR. ARM ARM D8.7.5 requires ISB to synchronize FPCR writes. Forward-looking for Phase 5+ in-kernel FP (NEON memcpy / AES); today's eret to EL0 is context-synchronizing so not observable. Fix: `isb` after the FPCR MSR in context.S. **F168 (P3)**: `fp_enable_this_cpu` set FPEN but didn't mask CPACR's ZEN/SMEN/TTA. Architectural reset values are 0 (trap) so safe today; permissive firmware could leak non-zero through. Fix: `cpacr &= ~((3ull << 16) | (3ull << 24) | (1ull << 28));` before FPEN OR; `fp.cpacr_enabled` test verifies. 232 → 234 tests PASS × default + UBSan. **Audit-bearing per CLAUDE.md trigger surfaces (Scheduler + Initial bringup)**. Predecessor: R12-DMA (`f828649` / `bcb2ea4`).

- **Earlier tip**: **R12-gic-edge formal audit close landed — `dsb sy` after ICFGR write + extinction-on-bad-precondition + `g_max_intid` runtime bound (F200 + F201 + F204 + F205 closed; F202 + F203 deferred).** Closes the R12-gic-edge deferred audit (carried since P4-Ic5b2; self-audited at landing but formal pass deferred per CLAUDE.md trigger-surface discipline). Adversarial prosecutor surfaced 0 P0 + 0 P1 + **2 P2** + 3 P3. **F200 (P2)**: added `dsb sy` after the `GICD_ICFGR<n>` write in `gic_set_spi_edge_triggered` so the distributor's internal latching is observable before the subsequent `GICD_ISENABLER<n>` write in `gic_enable_irq` (ARM IHI 0069 §3.4.2 + Linux's GICv3 pattern). Without it, a strict GIC implementation could process ENABLE before the new edge config latches → first IRQ fires as level-triggered (storm). QEMU virt latches in zero time so not reachable today; forward-looking for Pi 5. **F201 (P2)**: converted `gic_set_spi_edge_triggered` from `bool` to `void` + `extinction()` on both failure preconditions (intid out of `[GIC_SPI_MIN, g_max_intid]` OR `g_dist_base == 0`). Both are kernel-internal-bug indicators — callers enforce via `kobj_irq_create`'s `intid >= 32` guard + `intid_try_claim`'s `g_max_intid` bound + boot ordering. Closes the R9-era rollback-discipline drift (the bool return was unchecked at the call site). **F204 (P3)**: `_Static_assert`s pin the ICFGR encoding's SBZ-bit-clear discipline (IHI 0069 §12.9.7) against future drift. **F205 (P3)**: exposed `u32 gic_max_intid(void)` accessor (runtime-discovered from `GICD_TYPER.ITLinesNumber`); tightened `intid_try_claim` to bound against `g_max_intid` rather than the architectural `GIC_NUM_INTIDS = 1020`. Without it, a `CAP_HW_CREATE` userspace caller could pass intid in `(g_max_intid, GIC_NUM_INTIDS]` and reach the GIC helpers with an unimplemented INTID → UNPREDICTABLE writes per IHI 0069 §12.9.7. **F202 (P3 deferred)**: ICFGR RMW SMP-safety — v1.0 serial-claim discipline holds; Phase 5+ concurrent driver-init revisit. **F203 (P3 deferred)**: stale `GICD_ICPENDR<n>` after edge-trigger re-claim — v1.0 doesn't exercise re-claim cycles. - **Earlier tip**: **R12-bss-2mib landed — kernel.ld assert tightened to encode the actual image + firmware ≤ 2 MiB L3 constraint.** The L3 mapping at `arch/arm64/mmu.c::build_page_tables` covers exactly the 2 MiB block `[kernel_2mib_pa, kernel_2mib_pa + 2 MiB)` where `kernel_2mib_pa = pa_kernel_start & ~(BLOCK_SIZE_L2 - 1)`. On QEMU virt with `KERNEL_LOAD_PA = 0x40080000`, that's `[0x40000000, 0x40200000)`; the 512 KiB firmware reservation sits inside (mapped invalid per R6-B F114), the kernel image follows. The original assert `(_kernel_end - _kernel_start) < 0x200000` checked image alone — allowing image_size up to 2 MiB while the real cap is 1.5 MiB with the firmware offset. P4-Ic7 fell off this cliff when image_size briefly grew from 1440 → 1572 KiB; P4-Jc preemptively shrank test-binary blob caps 128 → 96 KiB as a stopgap, leaving R12-bss-2mib as the canonical fix. New assert: `(_kernel_end - _kernel_start) + (KERNEL_LOAD_PA & (0x200000 - 1)) < 0x200000`. Linker evaluates the AND at link time (= 0x80000 = 512 KiB on QEMU virt); image cap becomes 1.5 MiB. If KERNEL_LOAD_PA ever moves to a 2 MiB boundary, the AND evaluates to 0 and the assert reduces to image-only `< 2 MiB` — no special-casing. Current image_size 0x14a000 (1320 KiB) + 0x80000 = 0x1ca000 under 2 MiB; 216 KiB headroom. New "Kernel image + firmware reservation must fit in a single 2 MiB L3 block" Caveat in `docs/reference/03-mmu.md` documents the constraint with three legitimate fixes if image > 1.5 MiB is ever needed: (a) reduce firmware offset; (b) extend build_page_tables to map a second 2 MiB block; (c) demote the L2 entry to multiple page-grain L3 tables. The P4-Jc bundled blob-cap shrink (96 KiB per test blob) is preserved as operational headroom for near-term growth — the load-bearing constraint is now the assert, not the cap discipline. **Audit-bearing at the kernel.ld / Initial bringup category** (CLAUDE.md trigger surfaces); self-audit clean: the assert IS the regression test. Closes the R12-bss-2mib deferred audit item. 231/231 PASS × default (~431 ms) + UBSan (~471 ms); 5/5 KASLR sample distinct. Predecessor: P4-Jc (`dbf1425` / `7ac0f2c`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P4-Jc landed — virtio-net-loop: steady-state RX recycling + TX descriptor reuse; foundation for 9P-over-TCP in Phase 5.** New userspace binary `usr/virtio-net-loop/` (~640 LOC Rust) closes the steady-state gap left by P4-Jb's single-shot probe. Two new mechanisms: (1) RX descriptor recycling — each consumed RX descriptor is re-published to the avail ring at `rx_avail_idx % QUEUE_SIZE` with wrapping bump; (2) TX descriptor reuse via pre-init static `descriptor[k] → buffer[k]` mapping; `avail.ring[k] = k` for k in 0..16; send_pending_tx just advances tx_avail_idx and the device cycles through descriptors as avail.idx grows. Target volume N = 24 round-trips through 16 descriptors on each side — proves descriptor wraparound on both TX (descriptor 0 reused at TX#17) and RX (descriptor 0 recycled after first frame consumed). In-flight guard `tx_avail_idx.wrapping_sub(tx_seen_used) < QUEUE_SIZE` enforces no-reuse-while-device-owns. Loop body: irq_wait → ack → drain_tx → drain_rx+recycle → send_pending_tx. u16-wraparound discipline on all 4 counters via `wrapping_add(1)` + `!=`. Compile-time `const _: () = { assert!(...) }` pins TX-pool fits in ring DMA. No new substrate (same composed hw-handle surface as virtio-net-arp). Wire validation: 24 ARP requests + 24 slirp replies bit-exact (`THYLACINE_NET_DUMP=path`). Bundled blob-cap shrink: all 8 test-binary blobs 128 → 96 KiB to keep image+firmware ≤ 2 MiB (largest binary is virtio-net-arp at 76 KiB; 20 KiB headroom per blob). Image_size: 1448 → 1352 KiB (net −96 KiB); 184 KiB headroom under image+firmware ≤ 2 MiB. pretouch_rodata_pages() pinned to page 1 (LOAD = 4974 B; objdump-confirmed). 230 → 231 tests. **Non-audit-bearing** at per-syscall layer; audit-bearing at userspace-driver discipline (self-audit clean). 231/231 PASS × default (~442 ms) + UBSan (~478 ms); 27/30 KASLR distinct. Predecessor: P4-Jb (`f53ad75` / `a084edb`).
- **Earlier tip**: **P4-Jb landed — virtio-net-arp: full ARP request/reply round-trip (first frame received from outside the guest).** New userspace binary `usr/virtio-net-arp/` (~590 LOC Rust) closes the wire-validation half left open by P4-Ja. Same composed hw-handle surface as P4-Ja plus a second `kobj_dma_create` (32 KiB) for a pool of 16 × 2 KiB RX buffers. Init configures BOTH virtqueues (RX=0, TX=1) before DRIVER_OK; 16 RX descriptors pre-published with VIRTQ_DESC_F_WRITE. After ARP TX kick, drains the RX used ring on each IRQ wake; first ARP reply with sender_ip=10.0.2.2 + target_ip=10.0.2.15 wins. Slirp's reply: sender_mac=52:55:0a:00:02:02 + opcode=2; observed end-to-end and verified bit-exact. **Key insight**: receiving a valid ARP reply is itself evidence the device delivered our TX frame — slirp wouldn't synthesize a reply otherwise. No separate TX-used.idx check needed (cleaner state machine). Single-buffer-per-frame mode (declined VIRTIO_NET_F_MRG_RXBUF). pretouch_rodata_pages() bounded to page 1 (LOAD spans 0..1; ~5.4 KiB; objdump-confirmed). Image_size: 1320 → 1448 KiB (+128 KiB blob); 88 KiB headroom remains under image+firmware ≤ 2 MiB. 229 → 230 tests. **Non-audit-bearing** at the per-syscall layer; audit-bearing at the userspace-driver discipline layer (self-audit clean). 230/230 PASS × default (~448 ms) + UBSan (~470 ms); 27/30 KASLR distinct.
